Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
The Nature of Faith and the Status of the Muqallid
Al-Nasafi states his view on faith and the muqallid, agreeing with Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's position on the definition of faith and why the muqallid is considered a believer despite being sinful for neglecting investigation.

Core Idea
Faith is heartfelt affirmation, and the muqallid is a believer yet sinful for abandoning reasoning.

Al-Nasafi begins by outlining his view on faith, which aligns with Abu Hanifa. He distinguishes between the essence of faith (tasdiq) and the worldly requirement (iqrar), and then addresses the status of the muqallid – one who follows without personal investigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of faith
Read the passage and note that Abu Hanifa defines faith as tasdiq (affirmation) and considers iqrar (confession) a condition for worldly rulings, not part of faith.
This is a key distinction in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the muqallid's status
Notice that the muqallid is considered a believer because his faith has the reality (haqiqa) of faith and is done earnestly for Allah, not out of compulsion.
However, he is sinful for not engaging in nazar and istidlal.
3
Recognize the scholarly support
Al-Nasafi notes that this position is reported from many early scholars, including Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and others.
This shows the view is not isolated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأي النسفي في إيمان المقلد وإيمان من عاين العذاب بعد الموت: يتحدث عن الإيمان فيقول بما قال به أبو حنيفة: "إن الإيمان هو التصديق، والإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام الدنيوية، والمقلد مؤمن لحصول الإيمان منه بركنه، وحقيقته، ولأن إيمانه كان تقربا إلى الله، وطلبا لمرضاته لا لدفع عذاب متوجه إليه، ولم يكن مضطرا، إلا أنه يجعله عاصيا بترك النظر، والاستدلال، وهذا القول محكي عن أبي حنيفة، والثوري، ومالك، والأوزاعي، والشافعي، وابن حنبل، وعبد الله بن سعيد القطان، والمحاسبي. ويذكر في أثناء الكلام رأي أبي الحسن الأشعري حيث يقول البغدادي: إنه وإن لم يكن مؤمنا على الإطلاق، إلا أنه ليس بكافر، ويقول النسفي: إن الأشعري وقع في مناقضة، لأنه أخرج المقلد من الإيمان ولم يدخله في الكفر، وعلى هذا فإن الأشعري يثبت المنزلة بين المنزلتين مثل المعتزلة، وأعتقد أن رأي النسفي والأشعري في إيمان المقلد قريبان ثم يذكر النسفي أقوال المعتزلة، ويبين أن أبا هاشم حكم بكفر المقلد ، وأن غالبية المعتزلة جعلوه فى منزلة بين المنزلتين، لأنه ارتكب كبيرة بتركه الاستدلال وعن إيمان من عاين العذاب في الآخرة فإنه يرى أن إيمانه غير نافع، لأن روحه خرجت من يده ولأنه آمن لمعاينة العذاب.
Al-Nasafi's view on the faith of the muqallid (imitator in belief) and the faith of one who witnesses punishment after death: He speaks about faith and says what Abu Hanifa said: 'Faith is tasdiq (affirmation), and iqrar (confession) is a condition for implementing worldly rulings. The muqallid is a believer because faith is obtained from him with its pillar and reality, and because his faith was a drawing near to Allah and seeking His pleasure, not to repel imminent punishment, and he was not compelled. However, he makes him a sinner for abandoning investigation (nazar) and inference (istidlal).' This statement is reported from Abu Hanifa, al-Thawri, Malik, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, Ibn Hanbal, Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, and al-Muhasibi. And he mentions during the discourse the view of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as al-Baghdadi says: 'Although he is not a believer absolutely, yet he is not a disbeliever.' And al-Nasafi says: Al-Ash'ari fell into contradiction because he excluded the muqallid from faith but did not include him in disbelief. On this, al-Ash'ari affirms the intermediate position (between belief and disbelief) like the Mu'tazila. I think the views of al-Nasafi and al-Ash'ari on the faith of the muqallid are close. Then al-Nasafi mentions the sayings of the Mu'tazila, and shows that Abu Hashim ruled the muqallid as a disbeliever, and that the majority of the Mu'tazila placed him in an intermediate position because he committed a major sin by abandoning inference. As for the faith of one who witnesses punishment in the Hereafter, he holds that his faith is not beneficial because his soul has left his hand and because he believed due to witnessing the punishment.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents al-Nasafi's view on the faith of the muqallid (one who adopts belief without independent investigation). He agrees with Abu Hanifa that faith is tasdiq (affirmation in the heart), while iqrar (verbal confession) is a condition for worldly legal rulings. The muqallid is a believer because his faith has the essential reality and is done as an act of worship seeking Allah's pleasure, not out of compulsion. However, he is sinful for neglecting nazar (investigation) and istidlal (inference). Al-Nasafi notes this position is reported from many early scholars. Then he discusses al-Ash'ari's view, as reported by al-Baghdadi: the muqallid is not a believer absolutely but not a disbeliever. Al-Nasafi criticizes this as contradictory, likening it to the Mu'tazilite 'intermediate position'. He personally thinks his own view and al-Ash'ari's are close. He then mentions Mu'tazilite views: Abu Hashim held the muqallid to be a disbeliever; the majority placed him in an intermediate state due to sin of abandoning inference. Finally, al-Nasafi holds that one who sees punishment in the afterlife and then believes gains no benefit because his belief is compelled by witnessing punishment.

Key Terms
المقلد
التصديق
الإقرار
النظر
الاستدلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Nasafi considers the muqallid's faith invalid or that he is a disbeliever.
Correction: Al-Nasafi explicitly affirms that the muqallid is a believer (mu'min) with valid faith, though he is sinful for not investigating.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what is the status of the muqallid?
A) He is a disbeliever because he lacks investigation.
B) He is a believer but sinful for abandoning investigation.
C) He is neither a believer nor a disbeliever.
D) He is a perfect believer without sin.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi affirms the muqallid's faith as valid but sinful for neglecting investigation, a view held by many early scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever critically examined the evidence for the core beliefs of your faith, or do you simply rely on what you were taught? Would you be willing to challenge your own assumptions today, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
Al-Nasafi rules that the muqallid is a believer but sinful for not investigating. What is your personal stance on this? Are you content being a muqallid in some matters, or do you feel a responsibility to seek deeper understanding? How will you respond to that accountability starting this week?
?
Consider your daily acts of worship: do you perform them out of genuine conviction that you have verified, or out of habit and imitation? If your faith were tested tomorrow, do you have reasoned grounds to hold onto it? What step can you take today to strengthen your own nazar and istidlal?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
5 min
Al-Ash'ari's View on the Muqallid and al-Nasafi's Criticism
Al-Nasafi presents al-Ash'ari's view and criticizes it as contradictory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's classification of the muqallid as neither a believer nor a disbeliever, and al-Nasafi's critique that this leads to an intermediary position like the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's view forces an intermediate state, contradicting the binary of faith and disbelief.

Al-Nasafi now turns to al-Ash'ari's view, as reported by al-Baghdadi. Al-Ash'ari held that the muqallid is not absolutely a believer but also not a disbeliever. Al-Nasafi sees this as contradictory and equivalent to the Mu'tazilite 'manzila bayn al-manzilatayn' (intermediate position).

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ash'ari's position
According to al-Baghdadi, al-Ash'ari says the muqallid is neither a believer absolutely nor a disbeliever.
2
Understand al-Nasafi's criticism
Al-Nasafi argues that this is contradictory: excluding from faith without including in disbelief implicitly affirms an intermediate state.
He likens it to the Mu'tazilite doctrine.
3
Note al-Nasafi's personal opinion
Al-Nasafi considers his own view and al-Ash'ari's to be close.
This nuance is important for later comparisons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأي النسفي في إيمان المقلد وإيمان من عاين العذاب بعد الموت: يتحدث عن الإيمان فيقول بما قال به أبو حنيفة: "إن الإيمان هو التصديق، والإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام الدنيوية، والمقلد مؤمن لحصول الإيمان منه بركنه، وحقيقته، ولأن إيمانه كان تقربا إلى الله، وطلبا لمرضاته لا لدفع عذاب متوجه إليه، ولم يكن مضطرا، إلا أنه يجعله عاصيا بترك النظر، والاستدلال، وهذا القول محكي عن أبي حنيفة، والثوري، ومالك، والأوزاعي، والشافعي، وابن حنبل، وعبد الله بن سعيد القطان، والمحاسبي. ويذكر في أثناء الكلام رأي أبي الحسن الأشعري حيث يقول البغدادي: إنه وإن لم يكن مؤمنا على الإطلاق، إلا أنه ليس بكافر، ويقول النسفي: إن الأشعري وقع في مناقضة، لأنه أخرج المقلد من الإيمان ولم يدخله في الكفر، وعلى هذا فإن الأشعري يثبت المنزلة بين المنزلتين مثل المعتزلة، وأعتقد أن رأي النسفي والأشعري في إيمان المقلد قريبان ثم يذكر النسفي أقوال المعتزلة، ويبين أن أبا هاشم حكم بكفر المقلد ، وأن غالبية المعتزلة جعلوه فى منزلة بين المنزلتين، لأنه ارتكب كبيرة بتركه الاستدلال وعن إيمان من عاين العذاب في الآخرة فإنه يرى أن إيمانه غير نافع، لأن روحه خرجت من يده ولأنه آمن لمعاينة العذاب.

The muqallid is a believer because faith is obtained from him with its pillar and reality, and because his faith was a drawing near to Allah and seeking His pleasure, not to repel imminent punishment, and he was not compelled. However, he makes him a sinner for abandoning investigation (nazar) and inference (istidlal).' This statement is reported from Abu Hanifa, al-Thawri, Malik, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, Ibn Hanbal, Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, and al-Muhasibi. And he mentions during the discourse the view of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as al-Baghdadi says: 'Although he is not a believer absolutely, yet he is not a disbeliever.' On this, al-Ash'ari affirms the intermediate position (between belief and disbelief) like the Mu'tazila. I think the views of al-Nasafi and al-Ash'ari on the faith of the muqallid are close. Then al-Nasafi mentions the sayings of the Mu'tazila, and shows that Abu Hashim ruled the muqallid as a disbeliever, and that the majority of the Mu'tazila placed him in an intermediate position because he committed a major sin by abandoning inference. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari and al-Nasafi hold completely opposite views.
Correction: Al-Nasafi himself says they are close, despite his criticism of al-Ash'ari's wording.

Checkpoint
What does al-Nasafi accuse al-Ash'ari of?
A) Being a Mu'tazilite
B) Contradiction by excluding from faith but not including in disbelief
C) Denying the faith of the muqallid entirely
D) Affirming that the muqallid is a disbeliever

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi criticizes al-Ash'ari for inadvertently adopting an intermediate position on the muqallid, though he sees both views as close.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you follow a religious teaching without truly understanding its evidence, do you consider yourself a believer? Al-Ash'ari's view on the muqallid challenges the status of your faith. Will you commit today to seeking knowledge so that your faith becomes a matter of conviction rather than imitation?
?
Al-Nasafi accused al-Ash'ari of falling into contradiction by creating a third category between faith and disbelief. Are there areas in your own life where you try to carve out a 'middle ground' in your obedience to Allah? What is one specific gray area you will abandon starting now?
?
The Mu'tazilites invented an intermediate position for those who sin. But this lesson warns that there is no safe zone between iman and kufr. Have you ever excused a sin by thinking 'I'm still a believer, so it's okay'? Today, repent from that excuse and reaffirm that faith demands action and consistency.

Mu'tazilite Views on the Muqallid
Al-Nasafi presents Mu'tazilite positions on the muqallid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two Mu'tazilite positions: Abu Hashim's ruling of disbelief and the majority's intermediate state.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila split on the muqallid: Abu Hashim says disbeliever, majority say intermediate sinner.

Al-Nasafi outlines the Mu'tazilite opinions on the muqallid. Abu Hashim held that the muqallid is a disbeliever because he lacks proper inference. The majority placed him in an intermediate state between belief and disbelief, considering his abandonment of inference a major sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify Abu Hashim's view
Abu Hashim ruled the muqallid a disbeliever (kafir).
This is the harshest position.
2
Identify the majority view
The majority of Mu'tazila placed the muqallid in an intermediate position (manzila bayn al-manzilatayn) because he committed a major sin by abandoning inference.
This view aligns more with al-Ash'ari's apparent position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأي النسفي في إيمان المقلد وإيمان من عاين العذاب بعد الموت: يتحدث عن الإيمان فيقول بما قال به أبو حنيفة: "إن الإيمان هو التصديق، والإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام الدنيوية، والمقلد مؤمن لحصول الإيمان منه بركنه، وحقيقته، ولأن إيمانه كان تقربا إلى الله، وطلبا لمرضاته لا لدفع عذاب متوجه إليه، ولم يكن مضطرا، إلا أنه يجعله عاصيا بترك النظر، والاستدلال، وهذا القول محكي عن أبي حنيفة، والثوري، ومالك، والأوزاعي، والشافعي، وابن حنبل، وعبد الله بن سعيد القطان، والمحاسبي. ويذكر في أثناء الكلام رأي أبي الحسن الأشعري حيث يقول البغدادي: إنه وإن لم يكن مؤمنا على الإطلاق، إلا أنه ليس بكافر، ويقول النسفي: إن الأشعري وقع في مناقضة، لأنه أخرج المقلد من الإيمان ولم يدخله في الكفر، وعلى هذا فإن الأشعري يثبت المنزلة بين المنزلتين مثل المعتزلة، وأعتقد أن رأي النسفي والأشعري في إيمان المقلد قريبان ثم يذكر النسفي أقوال المعتزلة، ويبين أن أبا هاشم حكم بكفر المقلد ، وأن غالبية المعتزلة جعلوه فى منزلة بين المنزلتين، لأنه ارتكب كبيرة بتركه الاستدلال وعن إيمان من عاين العذاب في الآخرة فإنه يرى أن إيمانه غير نافع، لأن روحه خرجت من يده ولأنه آمن لمعاينة العذاب.
Al-Nasafi's view on the faith of the muqallid (imitator in belief) and the faith of one who witnesses punishment after death: He speaks about faith and says what Abu Hanifa said: 'Faith is tasdiq (affirmation), and iqrar (confession) is a condition for implementing worldly rulings. The muqallid is a believer because faith is obtained from him with its pillar and reality, and because his faith was a drawing near to Allah and seeking His pleasure, not to repel imminent punishment, and he was not compelled. However, he makes him a sinner for abandoning investigation (nazar) and inference (istidlal).' This statement is reported from Abu Hanifa, al-Thawri, Malik, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, Ibn Hanbal, Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, and al-Muhasibi. And he mentions during the discourse the view of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as al-Baghdadi says: 'Although he is not a believer absolutely, yet he is not a disbeliever.' And al-Nasafi says: Al-Ash'ari fell into contradiction because he excluded the muqallid from faith but did not include him in disbelief. On this, al-Ash'ari affirms the intermediate position (between belief and disbelief) like the Mu'tazila. I think the views of al-Nasafi and al-Ash'ari on the faith of the muqallid are close. Commentary
This passage presents al-Nasafi's view on the faith of the muqallid (one who adopts belief without independent investigation). He agrees with Abu Hanifa that faith is tasdiq (affirmation in the heart), while iqrar (verbal confession) is a condition for worldly legal rulings. The muqallid is a believer because his faith has the essential reality and is done as an act of worship seeking Allah's pleasure, not out of compulsion. Then he discusses al-Ash'ari's view, as reported by al-Baghdadi: the muqallid is not a believer absolutely but not a disbeliever. Al-Nasafi criticizes this as contradictory, likening it to the Mu'tazilite 'intermediate position'. He personally thinks his own view and al-Ash'ari's are close. He then mentions Mu'tazilite views: Abu Hashim held the muqallid to be a disbeliever; the majority placed him in an intermediate state due to sin of abandoning inference. Finally, al-Nasafi holds that one who sees punishment in the afterlife and then believes gains no benefit because his belief is compelled by witnessing punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all Mu'tazila consider the muqallid a disbeliever.
Correction: Only Abu Hashim held that view; the majority placed him in an intermediate state.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Mu'tazila, why is the muqallid placed in an intermediate position?
A) Because he is a true believer
B) Because he committed a major sin by abandoning inference
C) Because he is a disbeliever
D) Because he has not heard the message

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila are divided on the muqallid: Abu Hashim deems him a disbeliever, while the majority place him in an intermediate state due to his sin of abandoning inference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you follow a religious scholar without seeking the evidence yourself, do you consider yourself a muqallid? How does the Mu'tazilite classification of the muqallid as at least a grave sinner challenge your comfort in blind following?
?
If the majority of the Mu'tazila placed the muqallid in an intermediate state, what does that imply about the seriousness of investigating your beliefs? Are you willing to examine where you personally rely on evidence versus mere imitation?
?
Standing before Allah, would you be able to defend your core beliefs as derived from proof, or would they be based on what 'people say'? What would you say to the Mu'tazilite claim that abandoning inference is a major sin, even if you do not accept their doctrine?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
4 min
Faith of One Who Witnesses Punishment
Al-Nasafi rules on the faith of one who witnesses punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's ruling that faith compelled by witnessing punishment is not beneficial.

Core Idea
Faith born from witnessing punishment is invalid because it is compelled.

Al-Nasafi addresses the case of one who sees the punishment of the afterlife and then believes. He holds that such faith is not beneficial because it is the result of compulsion and hence not true faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the case
The person witnesses the punishment of the Hereafter and then believes.
2
Understand al-Nasafi's ruling
Al-Nasafi says this faith is not beneficial because the belief is compelled by witnessing the punishment, and the soul has left the body (i.e., it's too late).
This echoes the Quranic verse about faith at the time of death not being accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأي النسفي في إيمان المقلد وإيمان من عاين العذاب بعد الموت: يتحدث عن الإيمان فيقول بما قال به أبو حنيفة: "إن الإيمان هو التصديق، والإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام الدنيوية، والمقلد مؤمن لحصول الإيمان منه بركنه، وحقيقته، ولأن إيمانه كان تقربا إلى الله، وطلبا لمرضاته لا لدفع عذاب متوجه إليه، ولم يكن مضطرا، إلا أنه يجعله عاصيا بترك النظر، والاستدلال، وهذا القول محكي عن أبي حنيفة، والثوري، ومالك، والأوزاعي، والشافعي، وابن حنبل، وعبد الله بن سعيد القطان، والمحاسبي. ويذكر في أثناء الكلام رأي أبي الحسن الأشعري حيث يقول البغدادي: إنه وإن لم يكن مؤمنا على الإطلاق، إلا أنه ليس بكافر، ويقول النسفي: إن الأشعري وقع في مناقضة، لأنه أخرج المقلد من الإيمان ولم يدخله في الكفر، وعلى هذا فإن الأشعري يثبت المنزلة بين المنزلتين مثل المعتزلة، وأعتقد أن رأي النسفي والأشعري في إيمان المقلد قريبان ثم يذكر النسفي أقوال المعتزلة، ويبين أن أبا هاشم حكم بكفر المقلد ، وأن غالبية المعتزلة جعلوه فى منزلة بين المنزلتين، لأنه ارتكب كبيرة بتركه الاستدلال وعن إيمان من عاين العذاب في الآخرة فإنه يرى أن إيمانه غير نافع، لأن روحه خرجت من يده ولأنه آمن لمعاينة العذاب.
Al-Nasafi's view on the faith of the muqallid (imitator in belief) and the faith of one who witnesses punishment after death: He speaks about faith and says what Abu Hanifa said: 'Faith is tasdiq (affirmation), and iqrar (confession) is a condition for implementing worldly rulings. The muqallid is a believer because faith is obtained from him with its pillar and reality, and because his faith was a drawing near to Allah and seeking His pleasure, not to repel imminent punishment, and he was not compelled. However, he makes him a sinner for abandoning investigation (nazar) and inference (istidlal).' This statement is reported from Abu Hanifa, al-Thawri, Malik, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, Ibn Hanbal, Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, and al-Muhasibi. And he mentions during the discourse the view of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as al-Baghdadi says: 'Although he is not a believer absolutely, yet he is not a disbeliever.' And al-Nasafi says: Al-Ash'ari fell into contradiction because he excluded the muqallid from faith but did not include him in disbelief. On this, al-Ash'ari affirms the intermediate position (between belief and disbelief) like the Mu'tazila. I think the views of al-Nasafi and al-Ash'ari on the faith of the muqallid are close. Then al-Nasafi mentions the sayings of the Mu'tazila, and shows that Abu Hashim ruled the muqallid as a disbeliever, and that the majority of the Mu'tazila placed him in an intermediate position because he committed a major sin by abandoning inference. As for the faith of one who witnesses punishment in the Hereafter, he holds that his faith is not beneficial because his soul has left his hand and because he believed due to witnessing the punishment.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents al-Nasafi's view on the faith of the muqallid (one who adopts belief without independent investigation). He agrees with Abu Hanifa that faith is tasdiq (affirmation in the heart), while iqrar (verbal confession) is a condition for worldly legal rulings. The muqallid is a believer because his faith has the essential reality and is done as an act of worship seeking Allah's pleasure, not out of compulsion. However, he is sinful for neglecting nazar (investigation) and istidlal (inference). Al-Nasafi notes this position is reported from many early scholars. Then he discusses al-Ash'ari's view, as reported by al-Baghdadi: the muqallid is not a believer absolutely but not a disbeliever. Al-Nasafi criticizes this as contradictory, likening it to the Mu'tazilite 'intermediate position'. He personally thinks his own view and al-Ash'ari's are close. He then mentions Mu'tazilite views: Abu Hashim held the muqallid to be a disbeliever; the majority placed him in an intermediate state due to sin of abandoning inference. Finally, al-Nasafi holds that one who sees punishment in the afterlife and then believes gains no benefit because his belief is compelled by witnessing punishment.

Key Terms
عاين العذاب
إيمان
نافع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any faith, even at the sight of punishment, is accepted.
Correction: Al-Nasafi holds that such compelled faith is not beneficial because it is not a free choice.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Nasafi consider the faith of one who witnesses punishment not beneficial?
A) Because the person is already a disbeliever
B) Because his soul has left his hand and he believed due to witnessing punishment
C) Because he did not perform good deeds
D) Because he was a muqallid

Key Takeaway
Faith born from witnessing punishment is not beneficial because it is compelled and comes too late.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew you would witness the punishment of the grave tonight, would your faith change? Al-Nasafi says that faith born from witnessing is not beneficial. Examine your current faith: is it based on conviction or merely on fear of what you have not seen? Are you relying on a faith that could become useless if you had to face punishment? Take a step today to strengthen your faith in the unseen.
?
Consider a sin you have committed that you think is small. If you were to be shown its punishment in the Hereafter, you would desperately believe. But that belief would not save you. How does this change your view of your reliance on deathbed repentance? Write one concrete action you will take this week to increase your faith in the unseen.
?
The phrase 'soul has left his hand' implies a moment of no return. Are you treating your current life as the only opportunity for sincere faith? What would it take for you to believe with the same certainty as if you had seen, but without seeing? Commit to one practice that increases your iman bil-ghayb this week.

Iman of the Muqallid According to Al-Nasafi
Al-Nasafi defines the iman of the muqallid and lists supporting authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's position on the faith of the muqallid and why he considers him a true believer despite being sinful for abandoning reflection and inference.

Core Idea
The muqallid is a true believer but sins by not using his intellect.

Al-Nasafi addresses an important question: Can a person who follows without personal investigation (taqlid) be considered a true believer? In this passage, he clarifies that such a person’s faith is valid in its essence, but he is still accountable for not engaging in reflection. He then lists major Sunni authorities who held this view.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Notice that al-Nasafi begins by citing Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the definition of iman
The passage states that iman is tasdiq (assent) and iqrar is a condition for worldly rulings. Understand this distinction.
Tasdiq is internal; iqrar is external.
3
Analyze the status of the muqallid
Why is the muqallid considered a believer? Because his faith is genuine and he seeks Allah's pleasure. Why is he sinful? Because he abandons nazar and istidlal.
4
Review the list of supporting authorities
Notice the names: Abu Hanifa, al-Thawri, Malik, etc. This shows that the view was widely accepted.
You may not need to memorize all names, but recognize the weight of scholarly consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأي النسفي في إيمان المقلد: يتحدث عن الإيمان فيقول بما قال به أبو حنيفة: 'إن الإيمان هو التصديق، والإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام الدنيوية، والمقلد مؤمن لحصول الإيمان منه بركنه، وحقيقته، ولأن إيمانه كان تقربا إلى الله، وطلبا لمرضاته لا لدفع عذاب متوجه إليه، ولم يكن مضطرا، إلا أنه يجعله عاصيا بترك النظر، والاستدلال، وهذا القول محكي عن أبي حنيفة، والثوري، ومالك، والأوزاعي، والشافعي، وابن حنبل، وعبد الله بن سعيد القطان، والمحاسبي.'
Al-Nasafi's view on the iman of the muqallid: He speaks about iman saying what Abu Hanifa said: 'Indeed iman is tasdiq (assent), and iqrar (verbal confession) is a condition for applying worldly rulings. The muqallid is a believer because iman occurs from him with its pillar and reality, and because his iman was drawing near to God and seeking His pleasure, not to ward off impending punishment, and he was not compelled. However, he regards him as a sinner for abandoning nazar (reflection) and istidlal. This saying is reported from Abu Hanifa, al-Thawri, Malik, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, Ibn Hanbal, 'Abd Allah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, and al-Muhasibi.'
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents al-Nasafi's view on the faith of the muqallid (one who follows without personal investigation). He adopts Abu Hanifa's definition: iman is assent (tasdiq) of the heart, while verbal confession (iqrar) is a condition for worldly legal rulings. The muqallid is considered a true believer because his faith is genuine in its essence and he seeks God's pleasure, not because he is compelled by fear. However, he is sinful for failing to engage in reflection (nazar) and inference (istidlal). The passage then lists numerous early authorities who held this same position, indicating it was a widespread Sunni view.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the muqallid is not a believer at all.
Correction: Al-Nasafi confirms that the muqallid is a genuine believer, though sinful for neglecting reflection.

B) He is a believer without sin
C) He is a believer but a sinner for abandoning reflection
D) He is in the station between belief and disbelief

Key Takeaway
The muqallid is a true believer in the sight of Allah, but he commits a sin by failing to engage in rational reflection and inference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever blindly trusted someone else's understanding of faith without verifying it for yourself? What specific step will you take this week to personally reflect (nazar) on one of your core beliefs?
?
You believe you have genuine iman, but are you content to remain a muqallid in matters where you could investigate? What is one Islamic topic you have only followed without proof, and how will you start your own istidlal today?
?
The muqallid's sin is in abandoning his intellect. Where in your life have you been lazy about using your mind for deen? If you were to stand before Allah tonight, would you be satisfied that you sought knowledge actively, or would you regret the years of taqlid?

Al-Nasafi's Critique of al-Ash'ari on the Muqallid
Al-Nasafi critiques al-Ash'ari's view and relates Mu'tazila positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi considered al-Ash'ari's view on the muqallid to be contradictory and how it paralleled the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn.

Core Idea
Excluding from faith without including in unbelief is a logical contradiction.

Al-Nasafi examines al-Ash'ari's position on the muqallid — one who follows authority without independent reasoning. According to al-Baghdadi, al-Ash'ari said such a person is neither a true believer nor a disbeliever. Al-Nasafi sees this as a self-contradiction that inadvertently adopts the Mu'tazilite intermediate stance. Let's explore the critique and the Mu'tazila positions that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Nasafi uses a critical tone.
2
Identify al-Ash'ari's position
According to al-Baghdadi, al-Ash'ari says the muqallid is not a believer absolutely but is not a disbeliever. What does this imply about his status?
3
Understand al-Nasafi's criticism
Al-Nasafi says this is a contradiction (munāqaḍa) because it removes the muqallid from iman but does not place him in kufr. Ask yourself: why is this a logical problem?
This criticism leads to the charge that al-Ash'ari adopts the Mu'tazilite intermediate position.
4
Contrast with Mu'tazila views
Note the two Mu'tazila positions: Abu Hashim says the muqallid is a disbeliever; the majority place him in the intermediate station because abandoning istidlal is a major sin.
Compare these to al-Ash'ari's view and al-Nasafi's critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويذكر في أثناء الكلام رأي أبي الحسن الأشعري حيث يقول البغدادي: إنه وإن لم يكن مؤمنا على الإطلاق، إلا أنه ليس بكافر، ويقول النسفي: إن الأشعري وقع في مناقضة، لأنه أخرج المقلد من الإيمان ولم يدخله في الكفر، وعلى هذا فإن الأشعري يثبت المنزلة بين المنزلتين مثل المعتزلة، وأعتقد أن رأي النسفي والأشعري في إيمان المقلد قريبان ثم يذكر النسفي أقوال المعتزلة، ويبين أن أبا هاشم حكم بكفر المقلد ، وأن غالبية المعتزلة جعلوه فى منزلة بين المنزلتين، لأنه ارتكب كبيرة بتركه الاستدلال
He mentions during the discussion the view of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as al-Baghdadi says: 'He is not a believer absolutely, yet he is not a disbeliever.' Al-Nasafi says: 'Al-Ash'ari fell into contradiction, because he excluded the muqallid from iman but did not include him in kufr. Thus, al-Ash'ari affirms the station between the two stations (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn) like the Mu'tazila. I think the views of al-Nasafi and al-Ash'ari on iman of the muqallid are close.' Then al-Nasafi mentions the sayings of the Mu'tazila, and clarifies that Abu Hashim judged the muqallid as a disbeliever, and the majority of the Mu'tazila placed him in a station between the two stations because he committed a major sin by abandoning istidlal.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents al-Ash'ari's view on the muqallid according to al-Baghdadi: the muqallid is neither a believer absolutely nor a disbeliever. Al-Nasafi criticizes this as a contradiction, since al-Ash'ari removes the muqallid from faith but does not place him in unbelief, effectively adopting the Mu'tazilite doctrine of 'al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn' (the station between two stations). The passage then notes that al-Nasafi considers his own view and al-Ash'ari's view to be close. It concludes with the Mu'tazila positions: Abu Hashim judged the muqallid as a disbeliever, while the majority of Mu'tazila placed him in the intermediate station because of the major sin of abandoning istidlal.

Key Terms
مناقضة
منزلة بين المنزلتين
مقلد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's view on the muqallid is distinct and not shared by other groups.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that al-Ash'ari effectively adopts the Mu'tazilite intermediate position (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn), showing overlap.

Checkpoint
What criticism does al-Nasafi level against al-Ash'ari's view on the muqallid?
A) He considers the muqallid a disbeliever
B) He contradicts himself by excluding from faith but not including in unbelief
C) He is too lenient on the muqallid
D) He follows the Mu'tazila in everything

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's exclusion of the muqallid from faith without declaring him a disbeliever is seen by al-Nasafi as a logical contradiction that mirrors the Mu'tazilite intermediate position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own practice of faith, do you rely on the reasoning of scholars without personally seeking certainty? The muqallid here is criticized for abandoning istidlal. When was the last time you truly questioned a belief you hold, or do you prefer the comfort of authority over the risk of doubt?
?
Al-Nasafi exposes a logical contradiction in al-Ash'ari's view. Are there areas in your life where you hold two incompatible ideas about your faith—such as thinking you are safe from disbelief while never actually affirming your belief with conviction?
?
The passage discusses an 'intermediate station' between iman and kufr. In your heart, do you ever feel that you are neither fully a believer nor a disbeliever? What would it take for you to move from that middle ground to certainty—and are you willing to pursue it?

Faith from Witnessing Punishment Is Not Beneficial
Al-Nasafi rules that faith from witnessing punishment is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why faith that arises from directly witnessing punishment in the Hereafter is not considered beneficial according to Maturidi theology.

Core Idea
Forced faith from witnessing punishment is not saving faith.

This lesson addresses a critical boundary in Islamic theology: when does faith count? Al-Nasafi explains that faith inspired by the direct sight of punishment is invalid because it lacks the element of free choice. We will examine the two reasons he provides and why they matter for understanding the nature of true iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the concise style and the two reasons given.
The passage is a single sentence but packs a lot of meaning.
2
Identify the two reasons
Find the two reasons al-Nasafi gives for why this faith is not beneficial. They are introduced by 'because' (li-anna).
The reasons are: (1) his soul has left his hand, (2) he believed due to witnessing.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider why the time of death and coercion invalidate faith. How does this relate to the broader Maturidi emphasis on choice and reasoning in faith?
This principle distinguishes true faith from desperate belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن إيمان من عاين العذاب في الآخرة فإنه يرى أن إيمانه غير نافع، لأن روحه خرجت من يده ولأنه آمن لمعاينة العذاب.
Regarding the iman of one who witnesses punishment in the Hereafter, he holds that his iman is not beneficial, because his soul has left his hand and because he believed due to witnessing the punishment.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a person who believes only after directly witnessing the punishment of the Hereafter. Such faith is declared non-beneficial (ghayr nāfiʿ) for two reasons: first, at that moment the soul has left his hand, i.e., the time of repentance has passed; second, he believed under duress of direct observation, not through free choice. True saving faith must be based on choice and reasoning, not on coercion.

Key Terms
إيمان
معاينة
عذاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any last-minute faith, even from fear of punishment, is accepted.
Correction: This passage shows that faith inspired by directly witnessing punishment is not beneficial; it must be based on choice and reasoning before the final moment.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, why is the faith of one who witnesses punishment in the Hereafter not beneficial?
A) Because he is already dead
B) Because his soul has left his hand and he believed due to witnessing
C) Because he did not declare faith verbally
D) Because he was a disbeliever before

Key Takeaway
Faith that arises from directly witnessing punishment is not beneficial because it lacks the freedom and timing required for true iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own faith, do you find it is motivated more by fear of punishment or by genuine love and conviction? How can you shift your reliance from fear to voluntary submission?
?
Think of a time when you were confronted with the reality of death or the afterlife. Did that moment increase your faith? If so, what does this lesson teach you about the lasting quality of that faith?
?
If all fear of punishment were removed from your heart, would your faith remain unchanged? What would that reveal about the foundation of your iman?

The Sunni Position on the Major Sinner
Nasafi states the Sunni view on the major sinner and contrasts it with other sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position on the major sinner and how it differs from the views of the Murji'a, Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
The major sinner remains a believer, his final fate rests with Allah's will.

This lesson introduces the central debate on the status of Muslims who commit grave sins. Imam al-Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Sunna view that such a person is still a believer, and then contrasts it with the positions of other early theological schools. This comparison highlights the distinctiveness of the Sunni perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice how Nasafi first defines the Sunni view, then mentions other groups.
The passage includes a commentator's interjection, which provides an alternative perspective on the Murji'a.
2
Identify the four sectarian positions
List the views of Ahl al-Sunna, Murji'a, Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Hasan al-Basri. Pay attention to the key terms used (believer, fasiq, hypocrite, disbeliever).
3
Compare the Murji'a position with Ahl al-Sunna
Notice the commentator's argument that the Murji'a are actually similar to Ahl al-Sunna on this issue. Consider why this might be controversial.
4
Summarize the Sunni view
State in your own words the Ahl al-Sunna position: the major sinner is a believer, his fate is in Allah's will, but eventually he will enter Paradise.

الكلام في الأسماء والأحكام والوعد والوعيد: هذا ما هو اسم مقترف الكبيرة من أهل القبلة؟ وما هو حكمه في الآخرة؟ على يجيب الإمام النسفي ذاكرا رأي أهل الحق أن من ارتكب كبيرة غير مستحل لها ولا مستخف بالشرع فهو مؤمن ، وحكمه أنه لو مات من غير توبة فهو بين مشيئة الله إن شاء عذبه وإن شاء غفر له، إلا أن ماله إلى الجنة. ويذكر أن المرجئة تقول : إن أحدا من المسلمين لا يعاقب على كبيرة. وأحسب أن هذا الكلام لو قارنته بموقفهم من الفريقين المتقاتلين في صفين وأن رأيهم أنهما مؤمنان إلا أن أمرهما في الآخرة إلى الله عز وجل يعذب من يشاء ويغفر لمن يشاء ومن هنا فإني أخرج بنتيجة تخالف النسفي، وتقول: إن المرجئة في هذا مثل أهل السنة يجعلون مرتكب الكبيرة في الآخرة بين مشيئة الله. والمعتزلة يسمونه ،فاسقا وحكمه أنه في منزلة بين المنزلتين، ولو مات قبل التوبة خلد في النار ولم ينفعه إيمانه. أما الخوارج فواضح أنهم يكفرونه ويقولون بأنه مخلد في النار، ويذكر الحسن البصري أن مرتكب الكبيرة منافق. ويبين النسفي أدلة كل فريق من المخالفين، وبعد ذلك يذكر أدلة أهل السنة التي تؤكد أن مرتكب الكبيرة مؤمن إلا أنه في الآخرة بين مشيئة الله عز وجل. من ذلك أن الإيمان هو التصديق وضده التكذيب فما لم يتبدل التصديق بالتكذيب تكون الذات مؤمنة، لأن أهل السنة لا يثبتون الواسطة أما إذا انتقل التصديق إلى مرحلة الشك فهنا يكون الكفر. ويناقش النسفي رأي كل فريق على حدة ليبطله مثبتا أن المعتزلة هم الذين خالفوا الأمة بإحداثهم القول بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين. ثم إن الله سبحانه وتعالى أبقى اسم الإيمان مع وجود ما عليه الوعيد على سبيل المثال قوله تعالى: وَإِن طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا الحجرات: ٩] فلقد أطلق سبحانه اسم الإيمان عليهما مع أن فيهما حتما طائفة باغية. ثم إن الأمة أجمعت على الصلاة على من مات من أهل القبلة والاستغفار لهم ، من غير البحث في أحوال الميت هل ارتكب كبيرة أم لم يرتكب. ثم إن الله تعالى قد وعد بأن الحسنة بعشرة أمثالها، والمعتزلة لا يجوزون الخلف في الوعيد فكيف يجوزون الخلف في الوعد مع أن الخلف في الوعد مذموم والخلف في الوعيد محمود؟ ثم إن على كلام المعتزلة فإن الله يجازي بالسيئة ما لا نهاية له من العذاب وهو في الحسنة يبخل
Discussion on names, judgments, promise and threat: What is the name of the committer of a grave sin from among the people of the qibla? And what is his judgment in the afterlife? Then Imam al-Nasafi answers, stating the view of Ahl al-Haqq: that whoever commits a grave sin without deeming it lawful or belittling the Sharia is a believer, and his judgment is that if he dies without repentance, he is under God's will: if He wills, He punishes him, and if He wills, He forgives him, except that his final abode is Paradise. He mentions that the Murji'a say that none of the Muslims will be punished for a grave sin. I think that if you compare this statement with their position on the two fighting groups at Siffin – that their view is that both are believers, but their affair in the afterlife is up to God, He punishes whom He wills and forgives whom He wills – from here I reach a conclusion contrary to al-Nasafi, and I say that the Murji'a in this are like Ahl al-Sunna: they place the committer of a grave sin in the afterlife under God's will. The Mu'tazila call him 'fasiq' and his judgment is that he is in a station between the two stations, and if he dies before repentance, he will be eternally in the Fire and his faith will not benefit him. As for the Khawarij, it is clear that they declare him a disbeliever and say he will be eternally in the Fire. Al-Hasan al-Basri mentions that the committer of a grave sin is a hypocrite. Al-Nasafi explains the proofs of each opposing group, and after that he mentions the proofs of Ahl al-Sunna which affirm that the committer of a grave sin is a believer, but in the afterlife he is under God's will. Among that is that faith is affirmation (tasdiq) and its opposite is denial (takdhib); as long as affirmation does not change to denial, the person is a believer, because Ahl al-Sunna do not posit an intermediate state. But if affirmation turns to doubt, then that is disbelief. Al-Nasafi discusses the view of each group individually to refute it, affirming that the Mu'tazila are the ones who opposed the ummah by innovating the doctrine of the station between the two stations. Then God has preserved the name of faith despite the presence of what incurs threat, for example His saying: 'And if two parties among the believers fight, then make peace between them' [Al-Hujurat 9]; He applied the name of faith to both despite the fact that one party is necessarily transgressing. Then the ummah has unanimously agreed upon praying over anyone who dies from among the people of the qibla and asking forgiveness for them, without investigating the condition of the deceased whether he committed a grave sin or not. Then God has promised that a good deed will be rewarded tenfold, and the Mu'tazila do not allow breaking a threat, so how do they allow breaking a promise, while breaking a promise is blameworthy and breaking a threat is praiseworthy? Then according to the Mu'tazila, God would punish for a sin with endless torment while being stingy with reward for a good deed.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents the theological issue of the name and judgment of the major sinner among the people of the qibla. It is a comparative and argumentative passage. First, al-Nasafi states the view of Ahl al-Sunna (Ahl al-Haqq): a person who commits a grave sin without deeming it lawful or belittling the Sharia is still a believer. If he dies without repentance, his fate is in God's will—He may punish or forgive him, but his final destination is Paradise. Then the passage mentions the Murji'a view that no Muslim is punished for a grave sin. The commentator (author of the text) interjects, comparing the Murji'a position on the two fighting groups at Siffin where they considered both believers with their fate in God's will, concluding that the Murji'a are actually similar to Ahl al-Sunna on this point, contrary to al-Nasafi's claim. Next, the Mu'tazila view: they call such a person 'fasiq' and place him in a station between belief and disbelief, with eternal punishment if unrepentant. The Khawarij excommunicate him and consign him to eternal fire. Al-Hasan al-Basri even considers the major sinner a hypocrite. Al-Nasafi then provides proofs for Ahl al-Sunna: First, faith is affirmation (tasdiq); as long as affirmation remains, disbelief cannot be ascribed—there is no intermediate state between affirmation and denial; doubt would constitute disbelief. Second, God retains the name 'believers' for fighting parties in the Quran (Al-Hujurat 9), despite one being transgressors. Third, the consensus of the ummah is to pray over and seek forgiveness for any deceased Muslim regardless of sin. Fourth, God promises a tenfold reward for good, and breaking a promise is blameworthy, while breaking a threat is praiseworthy; the Mu'tazila's position would imply God breaks His promise and is stingy. The passage thus argues that Ahl al-Sunna's position is coherent and scripturally supported.

Key Terms

الإيمان
المرجئة
المعتزلة
الخوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna agree on the status of the major sinner.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna consider him a believer, not in an intermediate state; they reject the notion of a station between belief and disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunna, what is the ultimate fate of a major sinner who dies without repentance?
A) He is eternally in Hell
B) He is in Paradise after possible punishment
C) He is in an intermediate state
D) He is a hypocrite

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna affirm that a major sinner remains a believer, with his afterlife fate subject to God's will, and eventually he will enter Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly place yourself under God's will—hoping for forgiveness but fearing punishment—or do you assume leniency? How does the Murji'a mindset of 'no punishment' tempt you, and how can you resist it?
?
If you saw a Muslim committing a major sin, would your heart treat them as a believer or as an outcast? What would change in your attitude if you fully internalized the Sunni position that they remain a believer, yet their fate is in God's hands?
?
The Mu'tazila say the sinner's faith is useless without repentance. Do you rely on your faith alone while neglecting the need to repent? What is one major sin you have been procrastinating to repent from, and what is stopping you today?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Proofs for the Sunni Position
Nasafi presents four proofs for the Ahl al-Sunna position on the major sinner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key proofs Ahl al-Sunna use to support their position on the major sinner.

Core Idea
Faith is affirmation; major sinners retain faith, supported by Quran, consensus, and God's promise.

In this lesson, we examine the arguments al-Nasafi presents to justify the Sunni stance. These proofs are drawn from the definition of faith, a Quranic verse, the consensus of the ummah, and the nature of God's promises and threats. Together, they form a coherent defense of the view that a major sinner is not excluded from faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the proofs
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Identify each distinct proof al-Nasafi offers.
2
Understand the first proof
The proof from the definition of faith: faith is affirmation (tasdiq), and its opposite is denial. As long as affirmation remains, the person is a believer; there is no intermediate state. Doubt would constitute disbelief.
3
Analyse the Quranic proof
The verse from Al-Hujurat calls fighting parties 'believers', showing that even transgressors retain the name of faith.
4
Consider the consensus proof
The ummah prays over all deceased Muslims regardless of sins, indicating they are considered believers.
5
Reflect on the promise-threat argument
God promises tenfold reward; breaking a promise is blameworthy. The Mu'tazila allow breaking a threat but not a promise, implying inconsistency. The passage concludes that the Mu'tazila position would lead to God being stingy with reward.

Which of the following is NOT a proof used by al-Nasafi for the Ahl al-Sunna position?
A) Definition of faith as affirmation
B) Quranic verse about fighting believers
C) Hadith about intercession

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you secretly believe you have stepped out of the circle of faith? If not, why do you treat your sins lightly as if they have no effect on your relationship with Allah?
?
The Quran calls fighting believers 'believers' despite their transgression. Are you willing to extend that same recognition to a fellow Muslim who sins openly, or do you judge them as outside the fold? How does this lesson change your attitude toward those you consider 'major sinners'?
?
God promises tenfold reward for good deeds but may forgive sins. Are you living as if you can sin endlessly because God is merciful, or are you so afraid of His threat that you despair? Where is the balance in your heart right now, and what one step will you take today to move toward sincere repentance without losing hope in His mercy?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
The Definition of Iman: Affirmation, Not an Intermediate State
Nasafi defines iman as affirmation and rejects an intermediate state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunna define iman as affirmation (tasdiq) and reject an intermediate state between faith and disbelief.

Core Idea
Iman is affirmation; as long as affirmation remains, the person is a believer.

Nasafi begins his defense of the major sinner's faith by clarifying the very definition of iman. He argues that iman is simply tasdiq (affirmation of the heart), and its opposite is takdhib (denial). As long as affirmation is not replaced by denial or doubt, the person remains a believer—there is no third state.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify key terms
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the three key terms: tasdiq, takdhib, and wasita.
These terms are foundational for the entire debate.
2
Understand the no-intermediate-state stance
Ahl al-Sunna explicitly reject any intermediate state between faith and disbelief. This is a direct opposition to the Mu'tazila position.
3
Reflect on the implication for major sinners
Since sin does not replace affirmation, a major sinner remains a believer unless affirmation turns into doubt.
This definition is the first pillar of Nasafi's argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبين النسفي أدلة كل فريق من المخالفين، وبعد ذلك يذكر أدلة أهل السنة التي تؤكد أن مرتكب الكبيرة مؤمن إلا أنه في الآخرة بين مشيئة الله عز وجل. من ذلك أن الإيمان هو التصديق وضده التكذيب فما لم يتبدل التصديق بالتكذيب تكون الذات مؤمنة، لأن أهل السنة لا يثبتون الواسطة أما إذا انتقل التصديق إلى مرحلة الشك فهنا يكون الكفر. ويناقش النسفي رأي كل فريق على حدة ليبطله مثبتا أن المعتزلة هم الذين خالفوا الأمة بإحداثهم القول بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين. ثم إن الله سبحانه وتعالى أبقى اسم الإيمان مع وجود ما عليه الوعيد على سبيل المثال قوله تعالى: وَإِن طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا [الحجرات: ٩] فلقد أطلق سبحانه اسم الإيمان عليهما مع أن فيهما حتما طائفة باغية. ثم إن الأمة أجمعت على الصلاة على من مات من أهل القبلة والاستغفار لهم ، من غير البحث في أحوال الميت هل ارتكب كبيرة أم لم يرتكب. ثم إن الله تعالى قد وعد بأن الحسنة بعشرة أمثالها، والمعتزلة لا يجوزون الخلف في الوعيد فكيف يجوزون الخلف في الوعد مع أن الخلف في الوعد مذموم والخلف في الوعيد محمود؟ ثم إن على كلام المعتزلة فإن الله يجازي بالسيئة ما لا نهاية له من العذاب وهو في الحسنة يبخل في إعطاء مثلها - وهذا قمة المخالفة لنصوص القرآن وجعل القرآن متناقضا تعالى ربنا عن ذلك علوا كبيرا. ويذكر النسفي أن مرتكب الكبيرة المخلد في النيران هو المستحل لها والمستهين بأمور الشرع. ويفرق النسفي بين الكفر وبين ما ارتكب من الذنوب الأخرى من ذلك: أولاً: من عصى الله بنوع من الكبائر غير مستحل لها ولا مستهين بالشرع فهو مؤمن وما كان مستحلا ومستهينا فهو كافر لأنه منكر مكذب. ثانياً: أن الكفر مذهب يعتقد للأبد أما غيره فهو مرتبط بوقت الكبيرة وهو غلبة الشهوة لا للأبد وفي عقيدته العزم على التوبة.
And al-Nasafi explains the proofs of each opposing group, and after that he mentions the proofs of Ahl al-Sunna which affirm that the committer of a major sin is a believer, except that he is in the Hereafter under the will of Allah Almighty. Among that is that faith (iman) is affirmation (tasdiq) and its opposite is denial (takdhib); so as long as affirmation has not been replaced by denial, the essence remains a believer, because Ahl al-Sunna do not affirm an intermediate state, but if affirmation passes into the stage of doubt, then that is unbelief (kufr). And al-Nasafi discusses the view of each group individually to refute it, establishing that the Mu'tazila are the ones who opposed the community (umma) by innovating the statement of the station between the two stations. Then Allah Almighty preserved the name of faith despite the existence of what carries the threat (al-wa'id), for example His saying: 'And if two parties of the believers fight, make peace between them' [al-Hujurat 9]. For He Almighty applied the name of faith to them even though one of them is certainly a transgressing party. Then the community (umma) has consensus on praying over whoever dies from the people of the qibla and asking forgiveness for them, without investigating the state of the deceased—did he commit a major sin or not. Then Allah Almighty promised that the good deed (hasana) is multiplied tenfold, but the Mu'tazila do not allow breach in the threat (wa'id), so how can they allow breach in the promise (wa'd), while breach in promise is blameworthy and breach in threat is praiseworthy? Then, according to the Mu'tazila's statement, Allah would punish for an evil deed with endless torment, while in the good deed He would be stingy in giving its like—and this is the utmost contradiction to the texts of the Qur'an, making the Qur'an contradictory—exalted is our Lord far above that, a great exaltation. And al-Nasafi mentions that the committer of a major sin who is eternally in the Fire is the one who considers it lawful (mustahill) and is contemptuous of matters of the Shari'a. And al-Nasafi makes a distinction between unbelief (kufr) and other sins: First: whoever disobeys Allah by a type of major sin without considering it lawful and without contempt for the Shari'a is a believer; but whoever considers it lawful and is contemptuous is a disbeliever because he is a denier and rejecter. Second: that unbelief is a doctrine believed forever, while other sins are linked to the time of the major sin and are the domination of passion, not forever, and in his creed he is resolved to repent.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This long passage presents al-Nasafi's key arguments for the Ahl al-Sunna position that a major sinner remains a believer. The first argument is definitional: iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and as long as that affirmation is not replaced by denial or doubt, the person is still a believer—there is no intermediate state between faith and disbelief. Second, al-Nasafi uses the Qur'anic verse (49:9) where Allah calls two fighting parties believers, showing that sin does not negate the name of faith. Third, he invokes the consensus of the umma that Muslims pray over every deceased Muslim regardless of their sins, implying they are believers. Fourth, he makes an argument from God's promise and threat: God promised multiplication of good deeds, but if He fails to fulfill His promise, that would be blameworthy; yet the Mu'tazila allow failure in the threat while disallowing failure in the promise, which is inconsistent. Moreover, their position would imply that God punishes sins with infinite torment while being stingy in rewarding good deeds—a contradiction of the Qur'an. Al-Nasafi then clarifies that only the one who deems sin lawful and is contemptuous of the Shari'a is eternally in Hell. He then distinguishes kufr from other sins: a major sinner who does not deem the sin lawful is still a believer, whereas one who deems it lawful is a disbeliever because he is denying and rejecting. Also, kufr is a permanent belief, while other sins are temporary lapses where the person intends to repent. This distinction preserves the status of the believer despite grave sin.

Key Terms
التصديق
التكذيب
الواسطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that major sins automatically remove a person from faith entirely.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that as long as affirmation remains, the person is still a believer; sin does not negate faith.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what happens if a person's affirmation turns into doubt?
A) They become a hypocrite
B) They become a disbeliever
C) They remain a believer but sinful
D) They enter an intermediate state

Key Takeaway
Iman is affirmation; as long as it remains, the believer is still a believer even if he sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own heart, do you truly affirm the truths of Islam with certainty, or are there areas where subtle doubts linger? Nasafi says doubt is kufr—how does that challenge you to seek firm faith?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you feel your faith is lost? According to this lesson, as long as your affirmation remains, you are still a believer. Will you hold onto that truth and repent rather than despair?
?
There is no middle ground: you are either a believer or a disbeliever. Are you living as though you are fully committed, or do you act as if you are in a gray zone? What specific step will you take today to strengthen your affirmation?

Faith and Disbelief

Qur'anic Proof: Believers Who Fight
Nasafi uses Quran 49:9 to show sinners can be believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verse about fighting believers supports the view that major sinners remain believers.

Core Idea
Allah calls fighting parties 'believers' even though one is unjust.

Nasafi next invokes a direct Qur'anic proof. In Surah al-Hujurat, Allah addresses two fighting groups as 'believers' despite the fact that one of them is definitely a transgressor. This shows that sin does not negate the name of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Nasafi's comment
Read the Arabic of verse 49:9 and Nasafi's explanation that Allah preserved the name of faith despite the sin.
The verse explicitly uses 'al-mu'minin' for both groups.
2
Identify the implication
If sin removed faith, Allah would not call them believers. Therefore a major sinner can still be called a believer.
3
Connect to the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila denied this implication, but Nasafi uses the clear text.
This is a straightforward textual argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?
When you sin, do you still see yourself as a believer? Or do you feel that you’ve lost your faith? How does this verse change your view of yourself after sin? What action will you take to remind yourself that sin does not remove your title of faith, but still requires repentance?
?
If you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you treat them as a disbeliever or a believer? How does this verse guide your reaction? Write down one thing you will do differently the next time you encounter a Muslim in sin.
?
Are there sins you excuse because 'I’m still a believer'? How does the verse’s teaching about both faith and threat (al-wa'id) challenge that excuse? What is one sin you need to repent of now, and what step will you take today to turn back to Allah?

Consensus of the Umma: Praying Over All Deceased
Nasafi invokes the umma's consensus on praying over all Muslims, including sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus of the Muslim community on praying over every deceased Muslim supports the belief that major sinners are believers.

Core Idea
The umma prays over every Muslim regardless of sins, proving their faith.

Nasafi's third argument is based on the unanimous practice of the Muslim community. Muslims pray the funeral prayer (janaza) over every deceased person who professes Islam, without investigating whether they committed major sins. This consensus shows that the community considers them believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus statement
Read Nasafi's claim that the umma agrees to pray over every deceased person from the people of the qibla.
This includes both pious and sinful.
2
Understand the absence of investigation
The community does not inquire about the deceased's sins before praying; this implies they are believers.
If sin removed faith, such prayer would be invalid.
3
Reflect on the strength of consensus
Consensus is a strong proof in Sunni theology, showing the position is not a mere opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبين النسفي أدلة كل فريق من المخالفين، وبعد ذلك يذكر أدلة أهل السنة التي تؤكد أن مرتكب الكبيرة مؤمن إلا أنه في الآخرة بين مشيئة الله عز وجل. من ذلك أن الإيمان هو التصديق وضده التكذيب فما لم يتبدل التصديق بالتكذيب تكون الذات مؤمنة، لأن أهل السنة لا يثبتون الواسطة أما إذا انتقل التصديق إلى مرحلة الشك فهنا يكون الكفر. ويناقش النسفي رأي كل فريق على حدة ليبطله مثبتا أن المعتزلة هم الذين خالفوا الأمة بإحداثهم القول بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين. ثم إن الله سبحانه وتعالى أبقى اسم الإيمان مع وجود ما عليه الوعيد على سبيل المثال قوله تعالى: وَإِن طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا [الحجرات: ٩] فلقد أطلق سبحانه اسم الإيمان عليهما مع أن فيهما حتما طائفة باغية. ثم إن الأمة أجمعت على الصلاة على من مات من أهل القبلة والاستغفار لهم ، من غير البحث في أحوال الميت هل ارتكب كبيرة أم لم يرتكب. ثم إن الله تعالى قد وعد بأن الحسنة بعشرة أمثالها، والمعتزلة لا يجوزون الخلف في الوعيد فكيف يجوزون الخلف في الوعد مع أن الخلف في الوعد مذموم والخلف في الوعيد محمود؟ ثم إن على كلام المعتزلة فإن الله يجازي بالسيئة ما لا نهاية له من العذاب وهو في الحسنة يبخل في إعطاء مثلها - وهذا قمة المخالفة لنصوص القرآن وجعل القرآن متناقضا تعالى ربنا عن ذلك علوا كبيرا. ويذكر النسفي أن مرتكب الكبيرة المخلد في النيران هو المستحل لها والمستهين بأمور الشرع. ويفرق النسفي بين الكفر وبين ما ارتكب من الذنوب الأخرى من ذلك: أولاً: من عصى الله بنوع من الكبائر غير مستحل لها ولا مستهين بالشرع فهو مؤمن وما كان مستحلا ومستهينا فهو كافر لأنه منكر مكذب. ثانياً: أن الكفر مذهب يعتقد للأبد أما غيره فهو مرتبط بوقت الكبيرة وهو غلبة الشهوة لا للأبد وفي عقيدته العزم على التوبة.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever look down on a fellow Muslim who has committed a major sin, thinking they are less of a believer? How does the umma's unanimous practice of praying over all sinners challenge your heart to see them as brothers and sisters in faith? Will you commit to asking forgiveness for them instead of judging?
?
If you have committed major sins in the past, do you believe that Allah's mercy has already removed you from the community of believers? The umma's consensus shows you are still one of them. Do you truly accept that you belong, or do you still feel condemned? What would it take for you to stand confidently in your identity as a Muslim?
?
The sahaba did not investigate the sins of the deceased before praying over them. Do you investigate others' sins before treating them with respect and love? What would change if you followed this practice in your daily interactions?

Promise and Threat: A Rational Argument
Nasafi highlights the logical inconsistency in the Mu'tazila view of promise and threat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila position on promise and threat leads to contradictions, thus supporting Ahl al-Sunna view that major sinners remain believers.

Core Idea
If God cannot break His threat, He must also keep His promise—otherwise the Qur'an contradicts itself.

Nasafi now uses a rational argument based on God's promise (wa'd) and threat (wa'id). The Mu'tazila assert that God must fulfill His threat of punishment but allow that He may not fulfill His promise of reward. Nasafi points out the inconsistency: breaking a promise is blameworthy, but breaking a threat is praiseworthy. Moreover, if the Mu'tazila were correct, God would endlessly punish for a single sin while being stingy in rewarding good deeds—a clear contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the promise-threat passage
Read Nasafi's argument that God promised to multiply good deeds tenfold, but the Mu'tazila allow breach in promise while denying breach in threat.
Note the terms wa'd (promise) and wa'id (threat).
2
Understand the inconsistency
If God cannot break His threat, He also cannot break His promise. The Mu'tazila are inconsistent.
3
Reflect on the reductio ad absurdum
Nasafi shows that the Mu'tazila position implies God is unjust and the Qur'an is contradictory.
This strengthens the Ahl al-Sunna position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبين النسفي أدلة كل فريق من المخالفين، وبعد ذلك يذكر أدلة أهل السنة التي تؤكد أن مرتكب الكبيرة مؤمن إلا أنه في الآخرة بين مشيئة الله عز وجل. من ذلك أن الإيمان هو التصديق وضده التكذيب فما لم يتبدل التصديق بالتكذيب تكون الذات مؤمنة، لأن أهل السنة لا يثبتون الواسطة أما إذا انتقل التصديق إلى مرحلة الشك فهنا يكون الكفر. ويناقش النسفي رأي كل فريق على حدة ليبطله مثبتا أن المعتزلة هم الذين خالفوا الأمة بإحداثهم القول بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين. ثم إن الله سبحانه وتعالى أبقى اسم الإيمان مع وجود ما عليه الوعيد على سبيل المثال قوله تعالى: وَإِن طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَتَلُوا فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا [الحجرات: ٩] فلقد أطلق سبحانه اسم الإيمان عليهما مع أن فيهما حتما طائفة باغية. ثم إن الأمة أجمعت على الصلاة على من مات من أهل القبلة والاستغفار لهم ، من غير البحث في أحوال الميت هل ارتكب كبيرة أم لم يرتكب. ثم إن الله تعالى قد وعد بأن الحسنة بعشرة أمثالها، والمعتزلة لا يجوزون الخلف في الوعيد فكيف يجوزون الخلف في الوعد مع أن الخلف في الوعد مذموم والخلف في الوعيد محمود؟ ثم إن على كلام المعتزلة فإن الله يجازي بالسيئة ما لا نهاية له من العذاب وهو في الحسنة يبخل في إعطاء مثلها - وهذا قمة المخالفة لنصوص القرآن وجعل القرآن متناقضا تعالى ربنا عن ذلك علوا كبيرا. ويذكر النسفي أن مرتكب الكبيرة المخلد في النيران هو المستحل لها والمستهين بأمور الشرع. ويفرق النسفي بين الكفر وبين ما ارتكب من الذنوب الأخرى من ذلك: أولاً: من عصى الله بنوع من الكبائر غير مستحل لها ولا مستهين بالشرع فهو مؤمن وما كان مستحلا ومستهينا فهو كافر لأنه منكر مكذب. ثانياً: أن الكفر مذهب يعتقد للأبد أما غيره فهو مرتبط بوقت الكبيرة وهو غلبة الشهوة لا للأبد وفي عقيدته العزم على التوبة.
And al-Nasafi explains the proofs of each opposing group, and after that he mentions the proofs of Ahl al-Sunna which affirm that the committer of a major sin is a believer, except that he is in the Hereafter under the will of Allah Almighty. Among that is that faith (iman) is affirmation (tasdiq) and its opposite is denial (takdhib); so as long as affirmation has not been replaced by denial, the essence remains a believer, because Ahl al-Sunna do not affirm an intermediate state, but if affirmation passes into the stage of doubt, then that is unbelief (kufr). And al-Nasafi discusses the view of each group individually to refute it, establishing that the Mu'tazila are the ones who opposed the community (umma) by innovating the statement of the station between the two stations. Then Allah Almighty preserved the name of faith despite the existence of what carries the threat (al-wa'id), for example His saying: 'And if two parties of the believers fight, make peace between them' [al-Hujurat 9]. For He Almighty applied the name of faith to them even though one of them is certainly a transgressing party. Then the community (umma) has consensus on praying over whoever dies from the people of the qibla and asking forgiveness for them, without investigating the state of the deceased—did he commit a major sin or not. Then Allah Almighty promised that the good deed (hasana) is multiplied tenfold, but the Mu'tazila do not allow breach in the threat (wa'id), so how can they allow breach in the promise (wa'd), while breach in promise is blameworthy and breach in threat is praiseworthy? Then, according to the Mu'tazila's statement, Allah would punish for an evil deed with endless torment, while in the good deed He would be stingy in giving its like—and this is the utmost contradiction to the texts of the Qur'an, making the Qur'an contradictory—exalted is our Lord far above that, a great exaltation. And al-Nasafi mentions that the committer of a major sin who is eternally in the Fire is the one who considers it lawful (mustahill) and is contemptuous of matters of the Shari'a. And al-Nasafi makes a distinction between unbelief (kufr) and other sins: First: whoever disobeys Allah by a type of major sin without considering it lawful and without contempt for the Shari'a is a believer; but whoever considers it lawful and is contemptuous is a disbeliever because he is a denier and rejecter. Second: that unbelief is a doctrine believed forever, while other sins are linked to the time of the major sin and are the domination of passion, not forever, and in his creed he is resolved to repent.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This long passage presents al-Nasafi's key arguments for the Ahl al-Sunna position that a major sinner remains a believer. The first argument is definitional: iman is tasdiq (affirmation), and as long as that affirmation is not replaced by denial or doubt, the person is still a believer—there is no intermediate state between faith and disbelief. Second, al-Nasafi uses the Qur'anic verse (49:9) where Allah calls two fighting parties believers, showing that sin does not negate the name of faith. Third, he invokes the consensus of the umma that Muslims pray over every deceased Muslim regardless of their sins, implying they are believers. Fourth, he makes an argument from God's promise and threat: God promised multiplication of good deeds, but if He fails to fulfill His promise, that would be blameworthy; yet the Mu'tazila allow failure in the threat while disallowing failure in the promise, which is inconsistent. Moreover, their position would imply that God punishes sins with infinite torment while being stingy in rewarding good deeds—a contradiction of the Qur'an. Al-Nasafi then clarifies that only the one who deems sin lawful and is contemptuous of the Shari'a is eternally in Hell. He then distinguishes kufr from other sins: a major sinner who does not deem the sin lawful is still a believer, whereas one who deems it lawful is a disbeliever because he is denying and rejecting. Also, kufr is a permanent belief, while other sins are temporary lapses where the person intends to repent. This distinction preserves the status of the believer despite grave sin.

Key Terms
الوعد
الوعيد
الحسنة
السيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God must punish all sins without exception.
Correction: Nasafi shows that such a view leads to contradictions with God's promise and justice; God may forgive.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why is the Mu'tazila position on promise and threat inconsistent?
A) Because God cannot break His promise but can break His threat
B) Because breaking a promise is blameworthy, but breaking a threat is praiseworthy
C) Because God's promise is conditional
D) Because the Qur'an does not mention threats

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila position on promise and threat leads to logical contradictions; God may forgive major sinners without contradicting His word.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live more in fear of Allah's threat or in hope of His promise? Nasafi shows that breaking a threat can be praiseworthy. How does that affect your view of Allah's mercy toward your own sins? Will you now turn to Him with greater hope rather than despair?
?
When you sin, do you assume Allah must punish you, or do you trust that He may forgive? This lesson argues that binding Allah to His threat is inconsistent with His mercy. What would change in your daily obedience if you truly believed Allah's promise of reward is more certain than His threat of punishment?
?
Nasafi accuses the Mu'tazila of making the Qur'an contradictory by their position. Do you ever treat Allah's attributes as contradictory in your own heart—feeling that His justice and mercy cannot both be true? How can this passage help you hold both without forcing them into a human framework?

Distinguishing Kufr from Major Sins
Nasafi distinguishes kufr from major sins based on istihlal and contempt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the critical distinction between kufr (disbelief) and major sins, and why only those who deem sin lawful or show contempt are considered disbelievers.

Core Idea
Kufr is a permanent rejection, while major sins are temporary lapses with intent to repent.

Nasafi concludes by clarifying a crucial nuance: not all major sins make one a disbeliever. He distinguishes between the one who commits a sin while still affirming faith and the one who deems the sin lawful (mustahill) or shows contempt for the Shari'a. The latter is a true disbeliever, while the former remains a believer. Additionally, kufr is a permanent doctrine, whereas other sins are temporary and accompanied by a resolve to repent.

Guided Path
1
Read the distinction between mustahill and non-mustahill
Read Nasafi's statement: the one who commits a major sin without considering it lawful is a believer; the one who considers it lawful is a disbeliever.
Key terms: mustahill (one who deems lawful) and mustahin (contemptuous).
2
Understand the difference in nature
Kufr is an eternal belief system, while major sins are acts of disobedience that the person intends to repent from.
3
Reflect on the implications
This distinction preserves the status of believers who sin while condemning those who reject divine authority.

Faith and Disbelief
