Why the Imam Does Not Need to Be Infallible
Nasafi argues that infallibility is not a condition for the Imam, based on its exclusivity to prophets and the impossibility of verification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's rational and scriptural argument that requiring infallibility for the Imam is both impossible to verify and contrary to the Qur'anic principle of no burden beyond capacity.

Core Idea
Infallibility is a prophetic gift, not a political requirement.

In this passage, Nasafi directly addresses a key point of contention between Sunni and Shia theology: the condition of infallibility for the Imam. He argues that infallibility is a miracle-based quality exclusive to prophets, and that demanding it for the Imam would make the institution of leadership impossible. The argument combines rational reasoning with a Qur'anic verse to show that such a requirement would be an unbearable burden.

Guided Path
1
Read Nasafi's argument
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Nasafi states his position clearly: infallibility is not a condition.
Pay attention to the logical connector 'because' (لأن).
2
Understand the premise about miracles
Nasafi links infallibility to miracles (mu'jizat) that are outside the natural order. Ask yourself: why does this matter for the Imam?
Miracles are signs of prophecy, not ordinary human qualities.
3
Consider the practical problem
If we require infallibility, how would we ever know who is infallible? Nasafi says the community (mukallafun) cannot know it, so this requirement would stall the appointment of an Imam.
This is a rational argument about feasibility.
4
Connect to the Qur'anic proof
Nasafi cites Qur'an 2:286 to show that burdening people with an unverifiable requirement violates Allah's principle of not burdening a soul beyond its capacity.
The verse is a key scriptural foundation for this argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتكلم عن عصمة الائمة فيقول : إنها ليست بشرط، وذلك لأن العصمة مقترنة بمعجزات خارجات عن الطبائع، وهي خاصة بالأنبياء. والمكلفون بالاختيار لا يعرفون العصمة، وهذا يؤدي إلى تعطيل أمر هام، وهو الإمامة، وتكليف بما ليس في الوسع، مع أن الله تعالى يقول: لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٦].
Then he speaks about the infallibility (ʿiṣma) of the Imams and says: It is not a condition, because infallibility is connected to miracles (muʿjizāt) that are outside the natural order, and it is specific to the prophets. And those obligated with choice do not know infallibility, and this leads to the suspension of an important matter, namely the Imamate, and obligation of what is beyond capacity, even though Allah Almighty says: 'Allah does not burden a soul except its capacity' [Al-Baqara 286].
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that the Imam must be infallible (maʿṣūm). Nasafi explains that infallibility (ʿiṣma) is associated with miracles (muʿjizāt) which are outside the natural order (khārijāt 'an al-ṭabāʾiʿ), and it is exclusive to the prophets (khāṣṣa bi al-anbiyā'). Moreover, the people who are obligated to choose an Imam (al-mukallafūn bi al-ikhtiyār) cannot know if someone is infallible, because that knowledge comes through revelation and miracle, not through ordinary observation. Requiring infallibility would therefore lead to the suspension (taʿṭīl) of the institution of Imamate, as no one could be confirmed as infallible. This would be a burden beyond human capacity (takyīl bi mā laysa fī al-wusʿ), contradicting Allah's statement in the Qur'an: 'Allah does not burden a soul except its capacity' (2:286).

Key Terms
عصمة
معجزة
طبائع
أنبياء
تكليف ما لا يطاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Imam must be infallible (ma'sum) like the prophets.
Correction: Nasafi argues that infallibility is a prophetic quality tied to miracles, which cannot be verified by the community, and requiring it would make the Imamate impossible and violate the Qur'anic principle of no undue burden.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi argue that infallibility cannot be a condition for the Imam?
A) Because Imams are not prophets
B) Because infallibility is only known through miracles and is beyond human capacity to verify
C) Because the Prophet did not mention it
D) Because all Imams are sinful

Key Takeaway
Nasafi argues that infallibility is a prophetic quality, not a requirement for political leadership, and that demanding it would violate the Qur'anic principle that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life—marriage, parenting, leadership—are you unknowingly demanding 'infallibility' from others, holding them to a standard that only prophets could meet? How does the Qur'anic principle 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' invite you to release that expectation today?
?
Nasafi argues that the community cannot recognize infallibility, so demanding it would paralyze the institution of leadership. When you judge or criticize those in authority, do you assume you can fully know their inner state? How can this passage humble your tendency to make absolute judgments?
?
If infallibility is a prophetic quality linked to miracles, then expecting it from any human leader is not only unrealistic but a violation of divine mercy. What specific relationship or situation in your life would be transformed if you truly accepted that every person has limitations? Will you commit to naming one unrealistic expectation and letting it go this week?

The Definition of Iman as Tasdiq and Its Authorities
Definition of iman as tasdiq with citation of authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the foundational definition of iman according to the Maturidi school is tasdiq (affirmation), and you will know the key authorities who held this view.

Core Idea
Iman is tasdiq: affirmation of the heart, not mere actions.

This passage establishes the core definition of faith (iman) as affirmation (tasdiq), citing the founders of the major Sunni theological schools. Before we explore the implications, we must first grasp this fundamental understanding that unites the Maturidi, Ash'ari, and Hanafi traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first sentence to find the definition of iman as tasdiq. Notice that the author attributes it to Abu Hanifa.
2
Recognize the authorities
See that al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari also agreed on this definition. This shows the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna.
3
Understand the comprehensive nature
The author explains that affirming Muhammad (saw) includes affirming all tenets of faith. Reflect on how this single affirmation covers all beliefs.
4
Apply to all prophets
The same principle applies to every messenger and his community. This universalizes the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في إيمان المقلد: الإيمان هو التصديق على قول أبي حنيفة له كذا ذكره في كتاب العالم وهو اختيار الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي – رحمه الله وإليه ذهب أبو الحسن الأشعري وجماعة من المتكلمين، وهو على التحصیل تصدیق محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم بما جاء به من عند الله تعالى، إذ في هذه الجملة تصديق بجميع ما يجب التصديق به لأن فيه الإيمان بالله تعالى وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر، وبجميع ما يجب الإيمان به على التفصيل، وكذا في حق كل رسول مع أمته، ثم التصديق ينافي التكذيب والتردد، لما في التردد من التوقف، والمتوقف لا يكون مصدقا، وكذا المكذب ثم التصديق بحده إذا وجد فإن كان متعريا عما ينافيه من التكذيب والتردد كان الذات الذي قام به هذا التصديق مصدقا والتصديق هو الإيمان في اللغة، فمن كان مصدقا كان مؤمنا سواء وجد منه التصديق عن الدليل أو عن غير الدليل.
Discussion on the faith of the follower (muqallid): Faith (īmān) is affirmation (taṣdīq) according to the statement of Abu Hanifa—may Allah have mercy on him—as he mentioned in the book al-ʿĀlim wa l-Mutaʿallim. This is the choice of Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi—may Allah have mercy on him—and to it inclined Abu al-Hasan al-Ashʿari and a group of theologians (mutakallimūn). It is, upon verification, affirmation of Muhammad—peace be upon him—regarding what he brought from Allah Almighty, for in this statement there is affirmation of all that must be affirmed, because it includes faith in Allah Almighty, His angels, His books, His messengers, and the Last Day, and all that must be believed in detail. Similarly, in the case of every messenger with his community. Then affirmation contradicts denial and hesitation, because hesitation involves suspension, and the suspended person is not an affirmer, and likewise the denier. Then affirmation, by its definition, when it exists, if it is free from what contradicts it of denial and hesitation, then the entity in which this affirmation inheres is an affirmer (muṣaddiq). And affirmation (taṣdīq) is faith (īmān) in the language. So whoever is an affirmer is a believer, whether affirmation occurs through proof (dalīl) or without proof.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a definition of faith (īmān) specifically in the context of the muqallid (one who follows an authority without independent proof). The author begins by stating that the discussion is about the faith of the muqallid. He defines īmān as taṣdīq (affirmation/acceptance), citing Imam Abu Hanifa as the source, with agreement from al-Maturidi, al-Ashʿari, and many mutakallimūn. The definition is then specified: it is affirmation of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and what he brought from Allah. This comprehensive affirmation includes belief in God, angels, books, messengers, the Last Day, and all necessary details. The same applies to other prophets and their communities. Next, the author explains that taṣdīq inherently contradicts takdhīb (denial) and taraddud (hesitation). Hesitation implies suspension of judgment, which is incompatible with being a muṣaddiq (affirmer). Similarly, outright denial is incompatible. Then, the author clarifies the essential nature of taṣdīq: if the quality of taṣdīq exists in a person and is free from contrary elements like denial or hesitation, then that person is a muṣaddiq. And since taṣdīq is linguistically equivalent to īmān, that person is a muʾmin (believer). Importantly, this holds whether the taṣdīq comes from proof (dalīl) or not. This directly addresses the question of the muqallid: even without independent reasoning, if he possesses genuine affirmation, he is a true believer.

أبو الحسن الأشعري

B) Affirmation (tasdiq)
C) Knowledge (ma'rifa)
D) Verbal confession

Key Takeaway
Iman is fundamentally tasdiq (affirmation) of all that the Prophet brought, a definition upheld by the leading Sunni theologians.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage discusses the faith of a muqallid (follower). Is your faith a passive following of what you were taught, or an active, personal conviction? If you were asked to defend your belief in one specific tenet without relying on any authority, could you? Why or why not?
?
Do you sometimes measure your iman by your actions alone, feeling guilty when you fall short? The lesson teaches that iman is fundamentally affirmation. How does that truth reframe your relationship with Allah? What does it mean for how you view your own faith?

The Implications of Tasdiq: Denial, Hesitation, and the Muqallid
Explanation of tasdiq's implications and validity for the muqallid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tasdiq (affirmation) is incompatible with denial and hesitation, and that a person who possesses tasdiq is a believer even without independent proof (dalil).

Core Idea
Tasdiq alone suffices for faith; proof is not required.

Having established that iman is tasdiq, this passage now explores what tasdiq excludes and what qualifies a person as a believer. The author emphasizes that tasdiq cannot coexist with denial or hesitation, and crucially, that tasdiq remains valid whether it arises from proof or mere acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Discover what tasdiq negates
Read the part about tasdiq contradicting denial (takdhib) and hesitation (taraddud). Understand that both are incompatible with true affirmation.
2
Understand hesitation
The author explains hesitation involves suspension; a suspended person cannot be an affirmer. Reflect on why certainty is essential.
3
Learn the condition for being a muṣaddiq
Tasdiq, when free from its opposites, makes the person a muṣaddiq. This is a logical inference.
4
Conclude the ruling for the muqallid
The final sentence states that whoever has tasdiq is a believer, whether through proof or not. This directly includes the muqallid.

?

Or do you secretly doubt the validity of your faith if it is not backed by scholarly reasoning? Let go of the need for proof and accept the simple affirmation that Allah has placed in your heart.
?

Are you content with that? Or do you feel pressured to 'prove' your faith? Accept that your tasdiq is enough, and let that peace remove any insecurity.

The Faith of the Muqallid: Iman as Tasdiq
Nasafi defines iman as tasdiq and applies it to the muqallid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Abu Hanifa and the Maturidi school, the reality of iman is tasdiq (affirmation of the heart), and that the muqallid (one who believes without personal evidence) is a true believer because their affirmation suffices.

Core Idea
The muqallid is a believer because tasdiq, the heart's affirmation, is the essence of iman.

This lesson examines a foundational passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla, where he defines iman as tasdiq following Abu Hanifa, al-Maturidi, and al-Ash'ari. The passage argues that the reality of faith is free from denial and hesitation, and that this affirmation makes one a believer regardless of whether it arises from evidence or from simple acceptance. This directly addresses the status of the muqallid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own definition of iman come through clearly.
Notice that the passage begins by stating the position of Abu Hanifa and others.
2
Identify the core definition of iman
The passage defines iman as tasdiq (affirmation). Find the exact phrase where it says what tasdiq is directed towards. Understand that this tasdiq encompasses all required beliefs.
It specifies: 'affirmation of Muhammad (peace be upon him) regarding what he brought from Allah Almighty.'
3
Understand what tasdiq negates
The passage explains that tasdiq necessarily excludes denial (takdhib) and hesitation (taraddud). Consider why hesitation is incompatible with true affirmation.
Hesitation implies suspending judgment, which contradicts being a musaddiq (affirmer).
4
Apply to the muqallid
The passage concludes that whoever has tasdiq, even without evidence or in the state of witnessing, is a believer. See how Abu Hanifa's statement about disbelievers on the Day of Judgment supports this principle, and then apply it to the muqallid.
The muqallid's affirmation, though not based on personal evidence, is still true tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه - الكلام في إيمان المقلد : الإيمان هو التصديق على قول أبي حنيفة له كذا ذكره في كتاب العالم وهو اختيار الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي – رحمه الله وإليه ذهب أبو الحسن الأشعري وجماعة من المتكلمين، وهو على التحصیل تصدیق محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم بما جاء به من عند الله تعالى، إذ في هذه الجملة تصديق بجميع ما يجب التصديق به لأن فيه الإيمان بالله تعالى وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر، وبجميع ما يجب الإيمان به على التفصيل، وكذا في حق كل رسول مع أمته، ثم التصديق ينافي التكذيب والتردد، لما في التردد من التوقف، والمتوقف لا يكون مصدقا، وكذا المكذب ثم التصديق بحده إذا وجد فإن كان متعريا عما ينافيه من التكذيب والتردد كان الذات الذي قام به هذا التصديق مصدقا والتصديق هو الإيمان في اللغة، فمن كان مصدقا كان مؤمنا سواء وجد منه التصديق عن الدليل أو عن غير الدليل، وجد في حال الغيب أو في حال معاينة الغيب، ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة ، حيث قيل له ما بال أقوام يقولون يدخل المؤمن النار؟ فقال - رحمه الله -: لا يدخل النار إلا كل مؤمن، فقيل له: فالكفار ؟ فقال : هم مؤمنون يومئذ - كذا ذكره في الفقه الأكبر فقد جعل الكفار في الآخرة مؤمنين، لوجود الإيمان بركنه، إذ حقيقته التصديق وقد حصل، فعلى هذا كان المقلد مؤمنا لحصول الإيمان منه بركنه وحقيقته.
5 - Discussion on the faith of the muqallid: Faith is affirmation according to Abu Hanifa – thus he mentioned it in the book al-‘Alim, and it is the choice of Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah have mercy on him), and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari and a group of theologians went to it. And it is in summary the affirmation of Muhammad (peace be upon him) regarding what he brought from Allah Almighty, for in this sentence there is affirmation of all that is obligatory to affirm, because it contains faith in Allah Almighty, His angels, His books, His messengers, and the Last Day, and all that is obligatory to believe in detail, and likewise in the case of every messenger with his nation. Then affirmation negates denial and hesitation, because hesitation involves suspending judgment, and the one who suspends is not an affirmer, and likewise the denier. Then affirmation, by its definition, when it exists, if it is free from what negates it of denial and hesitation, then the entity in which this affirmation subsists is an affirmer, and affirmation is faith in language. So whoever is an affirmer is a believer, whether the affirmation comes from evidence or from other than evidence, whether in the state of the unseen or in the state of witnessing the unseen. For this reason Abu Hanifa said – when it was said to him: 'What about people who say that the believer will enter the Fire?' He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'None will enter the Fire except every believer.' It was said to him: 'What about the disbelievers?' He said: 'They are believers on that day.' – thus he mentioned it in al-Fiqh al-Akbar. He considered the disbelievers in the Hereafter as believers, due to the existence of faith with its pillar, for its reality is affirmation, and it has occurred. On this basis, the muqallid is a believer because faith has occurred from him by its pillar and reality.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage discusses the faith of the muqallid (the one who imitates without evidence). It begins by defining iman as tasdiq (affirmation), following Abu Hanifa, al-Maturidi, and al-Ash‘ari. The definition is: affirmation of Muhammad (peace be upon him) in all he brought from Allah, which includes all required beliefs. Then it explains that tasdiq necessarily excludes takdhib (denial) and taraddud (hesitation). Hesitation implies suspension of judgment, which is incompatible with affirmation. When affirmation is present and free from these negations, the person is a musaddiq (affirmer), and musaddiq linguistically means mu'min (believer). Therefore, a person is a believer whether their affirmation arises from evidence or not, and whether in the unseen or in witnessing. Abu Hanifa's statement about disbelievers on the Day of Judgment being 'believers' is cited: in the Hereafter, when they see the truth, they affirm, and since affirmation is the reality of faith, they become believers. Applying this, the muqallid who affirms without evidence is still a believer because the essential reality of faith (tasdiq) is present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith without evidence is invalid because it is not based on reasoning.
Correction: According to this passage, the reality of faith is tasdiq (affirmation). The muqallid's affirmation, even if not derived from evidence, is still genuine tasdiq, and therefore he is a true believer. Evidence is not a condition for the validity of faith.

Checkpoint

B) Affirmation (tasdiq) of what the Prophet brought
C) Performance of religious obligations
D) Belief based on evidence only

Key Takeaway
Iman is tasdiq (affirmation of the heart), and whoever has this affirmation, even without evidence, is a believer in the sight of Allah.

?

?
Abu Hanifa taught that even disbelievers will affirm on the Day of Judgment. How does this reality affect your urgency to call others to Islam, and how should you treat those who deny now?

Why Faith at the Sight of Punishment Does Not Benefit
Nasafi explains why faith at the time of witnessing punishment is not beneficial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why faith at the time of witnessing punishment is considered real but not beneficial in terms of reward or removal of punishment.

Core Idea
Faith at punishment's sight is real but useless—no evidence, no hardship, no reward.

Imam Nasafi tackles a subtle point: faith at the moment of doom is genuine affirmation, yet it brings no benefit. This seems puzzling until we consider the roles of evidence and hardship in earning reward. The passage draws on Quran 6:158 and Maturidi's insight to explain why such faith fails to save.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the distinction between the reality of faith (haqiqa) and its benefit (naf').
Notice that the author asserts faith exists but is not beneficial.
2
Understand the reason from Imam Abu Mansur
Identify Maturidi's interpretation: at the time of punishment, one cannot infer from the seen to the unseen, so the affirmation is not based on knowledge.
This explains why such faith is deficient despite being genuine.
3
Connect to the role of hardship
Note that reward is proportional to hardship; there is no hardship in simply acquiring basic faith at that moment, hence no reward.
This completes the explanation of why benefit is absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا ينفع إيمان من عاين العذاب]: ثم من وجد منه الإيمان عند اليأس أو عند معاينة العذاب، أو في الآخرة، لا يكون إيمانه نافعا على معنى أنه لا ينال ثواب الإيمان، ولا يندفع به عنه عقوبة الكفر، وهذا هو المَعْنِي من قول العلماء: إن الإيمان عند معاينة العذاب لا يصح أي لا ينفع فأما هو بحقيقته فهو موجود إذ الحقائق لا تتبدل بالأحوال، وإنما يتبدل الاعتقاد والأحكام، وما يتعلق به من العلائق ثم اختلفوا أن نفع الإيمان الحاصل عند البأس ومعاينة العذاب لماذا زال ؟ قال الشيخ الإمام أبو منصور - رحمه الله - في تأويل قوله تعالى يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ ايَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَتُهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ ءَامَنَتْ مِن قَبْلُ الآية : إن ذلك الوقت وقت نزول العذاب لا يقدر أن يستدل فيه بالشاهد على الغايب، ليكون قوله قولا عن معرفة وعلم، فعلى هذا لابد من أن يكون التصديق مبنيا على الدليل، فإذا تعرى تصديق المقلد عن الدليل لا يكون نافعا، وهذا لأن الثواب يكون بمقابلة ما يتحمله العبد من المشقة، ولا مشقة في تحصيل أصل الإيمان، بل
[The faith of one who witnesses punishment does not benefit:] Then whoever has faith at the time of despair or at the time of witnessing punishment, or in the Hereafter, his faith is not beneficial in the sense that he does not attain the reward of faith, nor is the punishment of disbelief repelled from him by it. This is the meaning of the scholars' statement: 'Faith at the time of witnessing punishment is not valid,' i.e., not beneficial. As for its reality, it exists, because realities do not change with states; rather, belief and rulings change, and the relations attached to them. Then they differed as to why the benefit of faith obtained at the time of distress and witnessing punishment is removed. Sheikh Imam Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said in interpreting the verse of Allah Almighty: 'On the day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before' (6:158): That time is the time of the descent of punishment; one cannot infer from the witnessed to the unseen, so that his statement would be a statement from knowledge and understanding. On this basis, affirmation must be based on evidence. If the affirmation of the muqallid is devoid of evidence, it is not beneficial. This is because reward is in return for the hardship the servant endures, and there is no hardship in obtaining the essence of faith. Rather...
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage discusses why faith at the time of witnessing punishment (such as at death or in the Hereafter) is not beneficial in terms of reward or removal of punishment. It first clarifies that such faith is real in its essence (tasdiq is present), but it does not benefit. The scholars say 'it is not valid' meaning 'it does not benefit'. Then it addresses the reason: Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi interprets Quran 6:158 to mean that at the time of punishment, one cannot use inference from the seen to the unseen (istidlal bi al-shahid 'ala al-gha'ib), so the affirmation is not based on knowledge. Therefore, the affirmations of a muqallid (one who imitates without evidence) are not beneficial either, because they lack evidence. The final reason given is that reward corresponds to hardship; there is no hardship in simply acquiring the basic faith at that moment, so no reward is earned.

Key Terms
معاينة العذاب
نفع الإيمان
الدليل
المشقة
الثواب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a person believes at the moment of death, that faith should save them and bring reward.
Correction: The passage explains that such faith is real but lacks the conditions of benefit: it is not based on evidence and there is no hardship, so it yields no reward and does not remove punishment.

Checkpoint
Why, according to Imam Abu Mansur, is faith at the time of witnessing punishment not beneficial?
A) Because the person is not sincere
B) Because at that time one cannot infer from the seen to the unseen, so the affirmation is not based on knowledge
C) Because the person has already committed major sins
D) Because faith requires a long period of practice

Key Takeaway
Faith at the time of witnessing punishment is real but not beneficial because it lacks evidential reasoning and hardship, both of which are necessary for reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What evidence do you personally rely on for your faith? If you were asked to explain why you believe, could you do so using reasoning from the seen to the unseen, or are you simply following? What specific step will you take this week to strengthen your conviction with evidence?
?
This lesson teaches that reward requires hardship. Reflect on your own life: what hardships have you endured for the sake of your faith? If the answer is little to none, does that concern you? What one act of worship or obedience that costs you something will you commit to starting today?
?
The faith of the muqallid (blind imitator) is said to be not beneficial. In which areas of your belief are you blindly following without understanding? How can you move from imitation to conviction? Identify one belief you will study until you are certain, and set a deadline for it.

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Iman as Tasdiq: The Muqallid is a Believer
Abu Hanifa defines iman as tasdiq and rules that the muqallid is a believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Abu Hanifa defined iman as tasdiq (affirmation of the heart) and that this definition leads to the ruling that a muqallid (blind follower) is considered a believer in the legal sense.

Core Idea
Faith is essentially inner affirmation, making the muqallid a believer.

This passage presents a foundational argument from Abu Hanifa on the nature of faith (iman). By analyzing his response to a challenging question, we see that the core of iman is tasdiq, inner affirmation. This has a direct consequence for the legal status of the muqallid, who affirms without independent evidence, yet is still counted as a believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the flow of the argument come through before interpreting.
Notice Abu Hanifa's paradoxical statement about disbelievers.
2
Identify the key question and answer
Find the question about the believer entering the Fire and Abu Hanifa's response. Then see the follow-up about disbelievers becoming believers on that Day.
3
Understand the reasoning: iman as tasdiq
The passage explains that iman in its essence (haqiqa) is tasdiq. This is why the disbelievers are called believers in the afterlife—they will have tasdiq at that moment.
This tasdiq does not benefit them, but it is still legally considered iman.
4
Apply to the muqallid
Since iman is merely tasdiq, the muqallid who affirms (even without evidence) has achieved tasdiq. Therefore, he is a believer according to Abu Hanifa's definition.
This shows that for Abu Hanifa, iman is not dependent on independent investigation (nazar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في حال الغيب أو في حال معاينة الغيب، ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة، حيث قيل له ما بال أقوام يقولون يدخل المؤمن النار؟ فقال - رحمه الله -: لا يدخل النار إلا كل مؤمن، فقيل له: فالكفار؟ فقال: هم مؤمنون يومئذ - كذا ذكره في الفقه الأكبر فقد جعل الكفار في الآخرة مؤمنين، لوجود الإيمان بركنه، إذ حقيقته التصديق وقد حصل، فعلى هذا كان المقلد مؤمنا لحصول الإيمان منه بركنه وحقيقته.
In the state of the unseen or in the state of witnessing the unseen, and for this Abu Hanifa said when it was said to him: 'What is with people who say that the believer enters the Fire?' So he said - may Allah have mercy on him: 'No one enters the Fire except every believer.' So it was said to him: 'Then what about the disbelievers?' He said: 'They are believers on that day' - thus it was mentioned in al-Fiqh al-Akbar. So he considered the disbelievers in the afterlife to be believers, due to the existence of faith (al-iman) with its pillar (rukn), since its essence (haqiqa) is tasdiq (affirmation) and it has occurred. Thus on this basis, the muqallid (blind follower) is a believer because faith has occurred from him with its pillar and essence.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of faith (iman) and applies it to the case of the muqallid. It begins by referencing Abu Hanifa's response to a question: some people claim that a believer enters Hell. Abu Hanifa counters that only every believer enters Hell. When asked about disbelievers, he says they will be believers on that Day, meaning in the afterlife when they witness the truth. This is recorded in al-Fiqh al-Akbar. The point is that faith (iman) in its essence (haqiqa) is tasdiq (affirmation of the heart), which will occur for the disbelievers at that time, so they are technically believers. However, this faith does not benefit them. The author then applies this reasoning to the muqallid: if faith is mere tasdiq, then the muqallid who affirms without evidence still has tasdiq, so he is a believer. Thus the passage establishes that iman is fundamentally tasdiq, and the muqallid's iman is valid for the legal judgment of being a believer.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-iman)
التصديق (al-tasdiq)
المقلد (al-muqallid)
الركن (al-rukn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the muqallid is not a believer because he lacks evidence.
Correction: The passage shows that iman as tasdiq is sufficient for the legal judgment of being a believer, so the muqallid qualifies.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Abu Hanifa consider disbelievers in the afterlife to be believers?
A) Because they will repent
B) Because they will have tasdiq (affirmation)
C) Because they will perform good deeds
D) Because they will escape punishment

Key Takeaway
For Abu Hanifa, iman is inner tasdiq, and even a muqallid who affirms without evidence is legally a believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have tasdiq in Allah—but does your life show it? When you sin, are you not contradicting the very affirmation you claim? What specific sin will you repent from today to make your tasdiq genuine?
?
On the Day of Judgment, the disbelievers will affirm the truth, but it won't help them. What is the difference between their tasdiq and yours? Is your tasdiq merely intellectual, or does it transform your actions?
?
The muqallid is saved by his simple affirmation—but you have more knowledge. Will you use that knowledge to deepen your certainty, or will you remain content with blind following? What is one step you can take this week to move from taqlid to yaqin?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
Faith at the Time of Punishment: Essence and Benefit
Maturidi defines the non-benefit of faith at punishment and asserts the unchanging reality of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith at the time of witnessing punishment is true faith in its essence, but it does not yield any benefit such as reward or removal of punishment.

Core Idea
Faith at punishment is real but benefits not.

Imam Maturidi begins this passage with a crucial clarification. When a person believes at the moment of despair or when the punishment is actually seen, scholars say that faith is not 'valid'—meaning it is not beneficial. However, he insists that such faith is still genuine faith, because theological realities do not change with circumstances. What changes are the rulings and benefits attached to it. Let us examine his precise wording.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening definition
Read the first part carefully. Note that faith at punishment is described as not beneficial, but in essence it exists.
2
Identify the distinction between essence and benefit
The author says 'fa amma huwa bihaqiqatihi fa huwa mawjud' — in its reality it exists. Understand that benefit is separate from essence.
3
Spot the question that leads to the disagreement
The passage ends with the question: why is the benefit removed? This sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من وجد منه الإيمان عند اليأس أو عند معاينة العذاب، أو في الآخرة، لا يكون إيمانه نافعا على معنى أنه لا ينال ثواب الإيمان، ولا يندفع به عنه عقوبة الكفر، وهذا هو المعني من قول العلماء: إن الإيمان عند معاينة العذاب لا يصح أي لا ينفع فأما هو بحقيقته فهو موجود إذ الحقائق لا تتبدل بالأحوال، وإنما يتبدل الاعتقاد والأحكام، وما يتعلق به من العلائق ثم اختلفوا أن نفع الإيمان الحاصل عند البأس ومعاينة العذاب لماذا زال؟ قال الشيخ الإمام أبو منصور - رحمه الله - في تأويل قوله تعالى يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ ايَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَتُهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ ءَامَنَتْ مِن قَبْلُ الآية: إن ذلك الوقت وقت نزول العذاب لا يقدر أن يستدل فيه بالشاهد على الغايب، ليكون قوله قولا عن معرفة وعلم، فعلى هذا لابد من أن يكون التصديق مبنيا على الدليل، فإذا تعرى تصديق المقلد عن الدليل لا يكون نافعا، وهذا لأن الثواب يكون بمقابلة ما يتحمله العبد من المشقة، ولا مشقة في تحصيل أصل الإيمان، بل المشقة في الوصول إليه بالاستدلال، ودفع الشبهة المعترضة بآداب الفكرة، وإدمان النظر والتأمل للتمييز بين الشبهة والحجج، فإذا صرف ذو البصيرة همته إلى التأمل والتفكر، وشغل قلبه وفكره بالبحث والتنقير ونظر بصدق العناية، وراعى شرائط النظر أتم الرعاية، وتحمل تلك المشقة، وتجشم تلك المرارة في ذات الله تعالى، وابتغاء مرضاته، نال الثواب ووصلت إليه منفعة إيمانه، وإذا جعل همته الوصول إلى اللذات الحاضرة، وخلى بين نفسه وبين الاستمتاع بالعاجلة، ثم آمن بلا تحمل مشقة، ولا لحوق مؤنة وكلفة، فلا ثواب له ولا ينال نفع الإيمان، كما لا ينال من آمن عند معاينة العذاب لانعدام الاستدلال من قبله، ثم لا فرق بين حصول الإيمان بعد التأمل والتفكر في أجرام العالم، ومعرفة حدوثها ومحدثها، ووحدانية محدثها، ومعرفة صفاته، وصحة الرسالة، وبين حصوله بالتأمل في أعلام الرسل ومعجزاتهم في تحمل المشقة وإتعاب النفس وآداب الفكر، فينال ثواب الإيمان الحاصل عقب التأمل في أعلام الرسل، وإن لم يتأمل في أجرام العالم وأجزائه، وإليه ذهب الشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفني والشيخ الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدي - رحمه الله - لقوله تعالى: يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ ءَايَتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَتُهَا والله الموفق. ثم قيل بأن زوال ثواب إيمان من آمن عند نزول العذاب، ووقوع البأس به، واندفاع نفعه عنه، إنما كان لأنه كان إيمان دفع العذاب لا إيمان حقيقة فلم يكن معتبرا فيما وراء قصد دفع العذاب أو لأنه كان محمولا على الإيمان عند تعلق
Then whoever has faith (iman) at the time of despair or at the time of witnessing the punishment, or in the afterlife, his faith is not beneficial in the sense that he does not obtain the reward of faith, nor is the punishment of disbelief repelled from him. This is the meaning of the scholars' statement that faith at the time of witnessing the punishment is not valid, i.e., not beneficial. As for it in its essence, it exists because realities do not change with circumstances; rather, belief and rulings change, and the attachments connected to it. Then they differed: why is the benefit of faith that occurs at the time of calamity and witnessing the punishment removed? Imam Abu Mansur (al-Maturidi) said in interpretation of His statement (the day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before) that that time is the time of the descent of punishment; one cannot infer from the witnessed to the unseen, so that his statement would be a statement based on knowledge and understanding. Therefore, affirmation (tasdiq) must be built upon evidence (dalil). So if the affirmation of the muqallid is stripped of evidence, it is not beneficial. This is because reward is in return for what the servant endures of hardship, and there is no hardship in obtaining the foundation of faith; rather, the hardship is in reaching it through inference (istidlal), repelling the intruding doubt with the disciplines of thought, and constant reflection and contemplation to distinguish between doubt and proofs. So when a person of insight turns his effort to contemplation and reflection, occupies his heart and mind with research and investigation, looks with sincere attention, observes the conditions of reasoning most fully, endures that hardship, undertakes that bitterness for the sake of Allah and seeking His pleasure, he attains reward and the benefit of his faith reaches him. But if he makes his goal the attainment of present pleasures, gives himself free rein to enjoy the immediate, then believes without enduring hardship or incurring trouble and cost, then he has no reward and does not obtain the benefit of faith, just like the one who believes at the time of witnessing the punishment due to the absence of inference on his part. Then there is no difference between obtaining faith after reflection and contemplation on the bodies of the world, knowledge of their temporality and their Creator, the oneness of their Creator, knowledge of His attributes, and the truth of prophethood, and obtaining it through contemplation on the signs of the messengers and their miracles in enduring hardship, tiring the soul, and the disciplines of thought. He attains the reward of faith that occurs after contemplation on the signs of the messengers, even if he did not contemplate the bodies of the world and their parts. This is the view of Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi - may Allah have mercy on them - due to His statement: 'The day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith.' And Allah is the Grantor of success. Then it was said that the removal of the reward of faith of one who believes at the time of the descent of punishment and the occurrence of calamity, and the repulsion of its benefit from him, is only because it was a faith to repel punishment, not genuine faith, so it was not considered beyond the intention to repel the punishment; or because it was based on faith when attached...
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage addresses why faith (iman) at the time of seeing punishment lacks reward. It clarifies that such faith is still true iman in essence because realities do not change with circumstances. The author then presents two explanations. The first, from Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, is based on the inability to use rational inference (istidlal) from the seen (shahid) to the unseen (gha'ib) at that moment: since the punishment is experienced directly, one cannot reason about the unseen, so faith is not based on knowledge. Therefore tasdiq must be built on dalil. The muqallid's faith without evidence is similarly not beneficial. Reward corresponds to hardship: there is no hardship in mere affirmation; hardship is in the intellectual effort of seeking evidence, confronting doubts, and continuous reflection. The passage describes this process: the person of insight (dhu basira) exerts himself in contemplation, investigation, and adab al-fikr to distinguish between doubt and proof; only then does he attain reward. The one who believes without such effort, as at the time of witnessing punishment, has no reward because no hardship was endured. Then it notes that there is no difference between reward earned through reflection on the cosmos and reflection on the signs of the messengers; both involve hardship. This view is attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and al-Maturidi. The passage then begins a second, incomplete explanation: the faith at punishment was merely to avert punishment, not genuine iman, so it is not considered beyond that purpose, or it was based on a different attachment.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-iman)
الثواب (al-thawab)
العذاب (al-adhab)
الحقائق (al-haqa'iq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that faith at the time of punishment is completely invalid or false.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that the faith itself is real – realities do not change – but it lacks benefit.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does it mean when scholars say 'faith at the time of witnessing punishment is not valid'?
A) It is not true faith
B) It is not beneficial
C) It is forbidden
D) It is incomplete

Key Takeaway
Faith at the time of punishment is genuine in essence but entirely lacks reward and cannot avert punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely heard that a deathbed conversion is accepted, yet this lesson teaches that faith at the moment of punishment is not beneficial. Does this shake your assumption about the safety of delay? What would it take for you to act on faith now, not when it is too late?
?
If your faith right now is genuine but not yet tested by despair, are you living as if its benefit depends on its timing? How can you ensure your iman is acted upon today rather than saved for a difficult moment?
?
The scholars say faith at punishment is real but useless. Have you ever felt sincere in a moment of fear but then returned to negligence? What keeps you from making your faith effective now?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
7 min
Maturidi's Explanation: The Necessity of Evidence and Hardship
Maturidi explains that lack of inference and hardship prevents reward for faith at punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's explanation for why faith at punishment lacks benefit: it is based on the inability to perform rational inference (istidlal) and the absence of hardship in seeking evidence.

Core Idea
Reward requires hardship of seeking evidence; at punishment, inference impossible.

In the previous lesson, we saw that faith at punishment is real but profitless. Now we delve into Imam Maturidi's reasoning. He argues that at the moment of punishment, one cannot infer from the seen to the unseen—the very basis of genuine faith. True faith must be built on evidence, and reward corresponds to the hardship of seeking that evidence. Since no such effort is possible at the moment of punishment, no reward can be earned. Let us trace his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's interpretation of the Quranic verse
He begins by referencing the verse that says faith at the coming of signs is not beneficial. Note his explanation that at that time, one cannot infer from the seen to the unseen.
2
Understand the role of evidence (dalil)
Affirmation (tasdiq) must be built on evidence. If it is not, as in the case of a muqallid or one who believes without inference, it is not beneficial.
3
Grasp the connection between reward and hardship
Reward is for the hardship endured. The hardship is in the intellectual effort of seeking evidence and overcoming doubts, not in the mere act of believing.
4
Note the comparison and the second explanation
The author says there is no difference between reflecting on the cosmos or on the signs of messengers; both involve hardship and yield reward. Then he begins a second, incomplete explanation about faith being merely to avert punishment.
The second explanation is cut off, so focus on Maturidi's main argument.

Key Terms
الاستدلال (al-istidlal)
المشقة (al-mashaqqa)
التصديق (al-tasdiq)
الدليل (al-dalil)
النظر (al-nazar)
الشبهة (al-shubha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that faith at punishment is still rewarded because it is faith.
Correction: Maturidi argues that reward requires the hardship of seeking evidence, which is impossible at that time.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the primary reason that faith at the time of punishment brings no reward?
A) The faith is not sincere
B) The person cannot perform rational inference
C) The punishment nullifies faith
D) The faith is based on fear

Key Takeaway
Faith that is not built on evidence and does not involve the hardship of seeking it cannot earn reward, as at the time of punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have believed in Allah your whole life, but when was the last time you truly endured the hardship of seeking evidence—sitting down to think deeply about His existence, attributes, or the truth of prophethood? If never, what does that say about the reward of your faith?
?
The passage says that blind faith (taqlid) without evidence is not rewarded. Are you willing to examine your own beliefs to see if they rest on evidence and effort, or are you comfortable with a faith that may bring no benefit in the Hereafter?
?
You claim to love Allah, but have you ever faced a doubt about your faith and disciplined your mind to resolve it through reflection? If not, what is preventing you from this struggle that the reward is tied to?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

The Reward of Bearing Hardship in Reasoning
Imam al-Maturidi describes the reward of faith attained through hardship in reasoning versus faith without hardship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why bearing hardship in reasoning (istidlal) is necessary for attaining the full reward of faith, and how faith without hardship is like faith at the time of punishment.

Core Idea
Hardship in seeking Allah unlocks the reward of faith.

This lesson delves into the first part of Imam al-Maturidi's argument. He begins by describing the intense effort required to reach correct belief through reasoning—repelling doubts, persevering in reflection, and enduring difficulty for Allah's sake. Only such faith, he argues, yields reward and benefit. In contrast, faith attained without any hardship, like that of a person who believes only when facing punishment, brings no reward.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on hardship and reward
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the vivid description of the effort involved: 'bearing that difficulty, enduring that bitterness for the sake of Allah.'
2
Identify the two contrasting scenarios
The passage presents two cases: one who exerts himself in reasoning and one who believes without hardship. Compare the outcomes: reward vs. no reward.
The author equates the latter with the one who believes at the sight of punishment.
3
Understand the connection to faith at punishment
Why does the author compare the one who believes without hardship to the one who believes at punishment? Because in both cases, faith lacks the prior effort of reasoning (istidlal).
This sets up the later defense of the muqallid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المشقة في الوصول إليه بالاستدلال، ودفع الشبهة المعترضة بآداب الفكرة، وإدمان النظر والتأمل للتمييز بين الشبهة والحجج، فإذا صرف ذو البصيرة همته إلى التأمل والتفكر، وشغل قلبه وفكره بالبحث والتنقير ونظر بصدق العناية، وراعى شرائط النظر أتم الرعاية، وتحمل تلك المشقة، وتجشم تلك المرارة في ذات الله تعالى، وابتغاء مرضاته، نال الثواب ووصلت إليه منفعة إيمانه، وإذا جعل همته الوصول إلى اللذات الحاضرة، وخلى بين نفسه وبين الاستمتاع بالعاجلة، ثم آمن بلا تحمل مشقة، ولا لحوق مؤنة وكلفة، فلا ثواب له ولا ينال نفع الإيمان، كما لا ينال من آمن عند معاينة العذاب لانعدام الاستدلال من قبله، ثم لا فرق بين حصول الإيمان بعد التأمل والتفكر في أجرام العالم، ومعرفة حدوثها ومحدثها، ووحدانية محدثها، ومعرفة صفاته، وصحة الرسالة، وبين حصوله بالتأمل في أعلام الرسل ومعجزاتهم في تحمل المشقة وإتعاب النفس وآداب الفكر، فينال ثواب الإيمان الحاصل عقب التأمل في أعلام الرسل، وإن لم يتأمل في أجرام العالم وأجزائه، وإليه ذهب الشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفني الشيخ الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدي رحمه الله لقوله تعالى: يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ ءَايَتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانُها والله الموفق. وإليه يشير أحد تأويلى وقيل بأن زوال ثواب إيمان من آمن عند نزول العذاب، ووقوع البأس به، واندفاع نفعه عنه، إنما كان لأنه كان إيمان دفع العذاب لا إيمان حقيقة فلم يكن معتبرا فيما وراء قصد دفع العذاب أو لأنه كان محمولا على الإيمان عند تعلق العذاب، أو لأنه عند تعلق العذاب الدنيوي به وهو مقدمة لعذاب الآخرة، إذ يموت بعذاب الدنيا، فينقل إلى عذاب الآخرة، خرجت نفسه من يديه إذ لا تقدر بعد ذلك على التصرف في نفسه، والاستمتاع بها، وشيء من هذه المعاني لم يوجد في حق المقلد، إذ إيمانه كان تقربا إلى الله تعالى، وطلبا لمرضاته، لا لدفع عذاب متوجه إليه، متشبث به إذ لا عذاب توجه إليه أو تشبث به، وكذلك لم يكن يلجأ إلى إيمانه مضطرا لانعدام سبب الاضطرار، وكذلك كانت نفسه في يديه لم يخرج منها وقد حصل منه الإيمان والله تعالى وعد الثواب على الإيمان، والثواب لا ينال إلا بفضل الله ووعده، فإذا وعد الثواب على فعل ينال فاعله الثواب سواء تحمل المشقة أو لم يتحمل، فلا ينعدم ثواب إيمان المقلد وإن لم يتحمل مشقة لتناول مطلق الوعد إياه، فأما إيمان من آمن دفعا للعذاب عن نفسه، أو كان ملجأ إليه، أو بعدما خرجت نفسه عن يده، فقد ورد النص بخروجه عن كونه نافعا، فقلنا بأنه لا ينفع، وفي الملقد اندفع هذا النص، وبقي مطلق الوعد على الإيمان، والشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله بين هذه المعاني الثلاثة لحرمان من آمن عند معاينة العذاب نفع الإيمان، فعلى هذا يكون هذا إشارة إلى أن المقلد لا يحرم نفعه لانعدام هذه المعاني عنه، والله الموفق.
The difficulty in reaching it through reasoning, and repelling the opposing doubt with the etiquettes of thought, and persistent reflection and meditation to distinguish between doubt and proofs. So when a person of insight turns his attention to reflection and meditation, occupies his heart and mind with investigation and scrutiny, looks with sincere care, observes the conditions of reflection with complete observance, bears that difficulty, endures that bitterness for the sake of Allah Most High and seeking His pleasure, he attains reward and the benefit of his faith reaches him. And if he makes his goal the attainment of immediate pleasures, leaves himself free to enjoy the fleeting world, then believes without bearing difficulty, without incurring trouble or hardship, then he has no reward and does not attain the benefit of faith, just as one who believes at the sight of punishment does not attain it due to the absence of reasoning before it. Then there is no difference between acquiring faith after reflecting on the bodies of the world, knowing their temporality and their Originator, the Oneness of their Originator, knowing His attributes and the truth of prophethood, and acquiring it through reflection on the signs of the messengers and their miracles in bearing difficulty, exhausting the soul, and the etiquettes of thought. So he attains the reward of faith acquired after reflection on the signs of the messengers, even if he did not reflect on the bodies of the world and their parts. And to this went the Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and the Shaykh Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi - may Allah have mercy on them - due to His saying, Most High: 'On the day that some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith.' And Allah is the Giver of success. And one of his interpretations points to this, and it was said that the removal of the reward of faith of one who believes at the descent of punishment, the occurrence of calamity upon him, and the repulsion of its benefit from him, is only because it was a faith of repelling punishment, not real faith, so it was not considered beyond the purpose of repelling punishment; or because it was based on faith at the time of the attachment of punishment; or because when the worldly punishment attaches to him and it is a prelude to the punishment of the Hereafter, as he dies by the worldly punishment and is transferred to the punishment of the Hereafter, his soul left his hands as he cannot after that dispose of himself or enjoy it. And none of these meanings exist in the case of the muqallid, for his faith was a drawing near to Allah Most High and a seeking of His pleasure, not to repel a punishment directed at him and clinging to him, since there is no punishment directed at him or clinging to him. Likewise, he did not resort to his faith under compulsion due to the absence of a cause of compulsion. Likewise, his soul was in his hands, it had not left him, and faith occurred from him. And Allah Most High promised reward for faith, and reward is only attained by Allah's bounty and promise. So when He promised reward for an action, the doer attains reward whether he bore difficulty or did not bear it. Thus the reward of the muqallid's faith is not nullified even if he did not bear difficulty, because the absolute promise encompasses him. As for the faith of one who believes to repel punishment from himself, or was compelled to it, or after his soul left his hands, the text has come that it is not beneficial, so we said it does not benefit. And in the compelled case, this text is repelled, and the absolute promise for faith remains. And Shaykh Abu Mansur - may Allah have mercy on him - explained these three meanings for the deprivation of benefit of faith for one who believes at the sight of punishment. So upon this, this is an indication that the muqallid is not deprived of its benefit due to the absence of these meanings from him. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument defending the reward of the muqallid (one who believes without personal reasoning) by distinguishing his faith from the faith of one who believes only at the sight of punishment. The author begins by describing the difficulty of reaching true faith through reasoning (istidlal), requiring persistent reflection and bearing hardship. When a person exerts himself in this way for Allah's sake, he attains reward and the benefit of his faith. Conversely, if one seeks only immediate pleasures and believes without any hardship, he neither receives reward nor benefit from his faith, just as one who believes only when facing punishment does not benefit because he lacked prior reasoning. The author then argues that there is no distinction in reward between one who arrives at faith by reflecting on the created world (heavenly bodies, their temporality, the unity and attributes of the Creator, and prophethood) and one who arrives at it by reflecting on the signs and miracles of the prophets. Both involve hardship, so both receive reward even if the latter did not reflect on the cosmos. The author cites Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Imam al-Maturidi, who invoke the Quranic verse (6:158): 'On the day that some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith.' This verse is used to argue that faith at the time of punishment is not beneficial. The author then enumerates three reasons why faith at the time of punishment lacks benefit: (1) it is only to repel punishment, not genuine faith; (2) it is based on faith at the moment of punishment's attachment; (3) when worldly punishment occurs, it is a prelude to the Hereafter, and the soul has left the person's control. None of these conditions apply to the muqallid, because his faith is a voluntary act of drawing near to Allah, not a response to imminent punishment or compulsion. The muqallid's soul is still in his hands, and he is not forced. Since Allah's promise of reward for faith is general, the muqallid receives reward even without the hardship of reasoning. The author concludes that Imam al-Maturidi explained these three reasons to show that the muqallid is not deprived of reward, as the factors that nullify benefit are absent in his case.

Key Terms
مشقة
استدلال
ثواب
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a person who believes without bearing any hardship?
A) He still attains reward but less than the one who bears hardship.
B) He attains no reward and no benefit from his faith.
C) He attains reward only if he believes in the prophets.
D) He attains reward because belief itself is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
Faith earned through sincere effort and hardship in reasoning is rewarded, while faith without effort brings no benefit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult question about your faith, do you tend to avoid the struggle or actively engage in reasoning? What does this passage say about that choice?
?
Think of a time when you believed something without questioning. Was that faith rewarded? How does this lesson challenge you to examine your own beliefs?
?
The passage describes bearing bitterness for the sake of Allah. What bitterness in seeking truth have you avoided? Will you commit today to embracing that hardship?

Faith and Disbelief

Two Paths to Faith: Reflecting on Creation or on Prophethood
Imam al-Maturidi argues the equivalence of reflecting on creation and on prophets for attaining reward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that reflecting on the signs of the prophets is equivalent to reflecting on the cosmos in terms of the reward earned through hardship.

Core Idea
The reward of faith depends on sincerity and effort, not the specific object of reflection.

In this lesson, Imam al-Maturidi addresses a potential objection: does the reward differ if one arrives at faith through contemplating the natural world versus through the miracles of the prophets? He argues that both involve hardship and sincere effort, so the reward is the same. He even cites the great scholars al-Rustughfani and al-Maturidi (himself) supporting this view, along with a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two paths
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. The author says there is 'no difference' between the two ways of arriving at faith.
2
Identify the two objects of reflection
One path is reflection on the bodies of the world (cosmos) leading to knowledge of the Creator; the other is reflection on the signs and miracles of the messengers.
Both involve 'bearing difficulty, exhausting the soul'.
3
Understand the supporting authority
The author cites Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, and the Quranic verse 6:158, to support the equivalence.
The verse is used to show that faith at the time of punishment is not beneficial, which indirectly supports the need for prior effort.

According to the passage, what is the basis for the equality of reward between reflecting on the cosmos and reflecting on the signs of the prophets?
A) Both require the same level of intellectual ability.
B) Both involve bearing hardship and exhausting the soul.

Key Takeaway
Reflection on the prophets' signs is a valid and rewarding path to faith, equivalent to reflecting on the cosmos.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely heard or used arguments from creation to strengthen faith. When you encounter someone who is more moved by stories of prophets and miracles, do you dismiss their path as less intellectual? How can you honor both paths as equally valid and rewarding, as al-Maturidi teaches, starting in your next conversation?
?
Reflecting on the prophets' signs often requires bearing difficulty and exhausting the soul. Have you ever truly exerted yourself in such reflection, or have you relied on a comfortable, ready-made faith? What specific step will you take this week to engage with the life of a prophet with genuine effort?
?
The Quranic verse warns that faith at the time of clear signs is not beneficial. Is your faith today the result of sincere reflection and effort, or are you waiting for a sign that will force belief? What change must you make now to ensure your faith is a genuine, hard-earned gift before it is too late?

Defending the Muqallid: Faith without Reasoning is Rewarded
Imam al-Maturidi defends the reward of the muqallid by distinguishing his faith from faith at punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi defends the reward of the muqallid by distinguishing his faith from the faith of one compelled by punishment.

Core Idea
The muqallid's sincere faith is rewarded, unlike forced faith.

The final part of the passage addresses a crucial question: what about the muqallid—one who believes without personal reasoning? Is his faith rewarded? Imam al-Maturidi argues that it is, because his faith is not a response to imminent punishment or compulsion. He explains three reasons why faith at the time of punishment is not beneficial, and shows that none apply to the muqallid. Thus, the general promise of reward for faith applies to him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the muqallid and the three reasons
Carefully read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three reasons given for why faith at punishment lacks benefit: it is for repelling punishment, it is compelled, or the soul has left control.
These reasons are based on the Quranic verse 6:158.
2
Compare with the muqallid
The author then lists why none of these reasons apply to the muqallid: his faith is for Allah's pleasure, not to repel punishment; he is not compelled; his soul is in his hands.
Thus, the muqallid qualifies for the general promise of reward.
3
Understand the overall argument
Imam al-Maturidi concludes that the muqallid is not deprived of benefit because the conditions that nullify benefit are absent. This supports the Maturidi position on the validity of taqlid in basic faith.

المشقة في الوصول إليه بالاستدلال، ودفع الشبهة المعترضة بآداب الفكرة، وإدمان النظر والتأمل للتمييز بين الشبهة والحجج، فإذا صرف ذو البصيرة همته إلى التأمل والتفكر، وشغل قلبه وفكره بالبحث والتنقير ونظر بَعْضُ ءَايَتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانُها والله الموفق. وإليه يشير أحد تأويلى وقيل بأن زوال ثواب إيمان من آمن عند نزول العذاب، ووقوع البأس به، واندفاع نفعه عنه، إنما كان لأنه كان إيمان دفع العذاب لا إيمان حقيقة فلم يكن معتبرا فيما وراء قصد دفع العذاب أو لأنه كان محمولا على الإيمان عند تعلق العذاب، أو لأنه عند تعلق العذاب الدنيوي به وهو مقدمة لعذاب الآخرة، إذ يموت بعذاب الدنيا، فينقل إلى إليه، متشبث به إذ لا عذاب توجه إليه أو تشبث به، وكذلك لم يكن يلجأ إلى إيمانه مضطرا لانعدام سبب الاضطرار، وكذلك كانت نفسه في يديه لم يخرج منها وقد حصل منه الإيمان والله تعالى وعد الثواب على الإيمان، والثواب لا ينال إلا بفضل الله ووعده، فإذا وعد الثواب على فعل ينال فاعله الثواب سواء تحمل المشقة أو لم يتحمل، فلا ينعدم ثواب إيمان المقلد وإن لم يتحمل مشقة لتناول مطلق الوعد إياه، فأما إيمان من آمن دفعا للعذاب عن نفسه، أو كان ملجأ إليه، أو بعدما خرجت نفسه عن يده، فقد ورد النص بخروجه عن كونه نافعا، فقلنا بأنه لا ينفع، وفي الملقد اندفع هذا النص، وبقي مطلق الوعد على الإيمان، والشيخ أبو منصور رحمه The difficulty in reaching it through reasoning, and repelling the opposing doubt with the etiquettes of thought, and persistent reflection and meditation to distinguish between doubt and proofs. So when a person of insight turns his attention to reflection and meditation, occupies his heart and mind with investigation and scrutiny, looks with sincere care, observes the conditions of reflection with complete observance, bears that difficulty, endures that bitterness for the sake of Allah Most High and seeking His pleasure, he attains reward and the benefit of his faith reaches him. And if he makes his goal the attainment of immediate pleasures, leaves himself free to enjoy the fleeting world, then believes without bearing difficulty, without incurring trouble or hardship, then he has no reward and does not attain the benefit of faith, just as one who believes at the sight of punishment does not attain it due to the absence of reasoning before it. Then there is no difference between acquiring faith after reflecting on the bodies of the world, knowing their temporality and their Originator, the Oneness of their Originator, knowing His attributes and the truth of prophethood, and acquiring it through reflection on the signs of the messengers and their miracles in bearing difficulty, exhausting the soul, and the etiquettes of thought. So he attains the reward of faith acquired after reflection on the signs of the messengers, even if he did not reflect on the bodies of the world and their parts. And to this went the Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and the Shaykh Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi - may Allah have mercy on them - due to His saying, Most High: 'On the day that some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith.' And Allah is the Giver of success. And one of his interpretations points to this, and it was said that the removal of the reward of faith of one who believes at the descent of punishment, the occurrence of calamity upon him, and the repulsion of its benefit from him, is only because it was a faith of repelling punishment, not real faith, so it was not considered beyond the purpose of repelling punishment; or because it was based on faith at the time of the attachment of punishment; or because when the worldly punishment attaches to him and it is a prelude to the punishment of the Hereafter, as he dies by the worldly punishment and is transferred to the punishment of the Hereafter, his soul left his hands as he cannot after that dispose of himself or enjoy it. And none of these meanings exist in the case of the muqallid, for his faith was a drawing near to Allah Most High and a seeking of His pleasure, not to repel a punishment directed at him and clinging to him, since there is no punishment directed at him or clinging to him. Likewise, he did not resort to his faith under compulsion due to the absence of a cause of compulsion. Likewise, his soul was in his hands, it had not left him, and faith occurred from him. And Allah Most High promised reward for faith, and reward is only attained by Allah's bounty and promise. So when He promised reward for an action, the doer attains reward whether he bore difficulty or did not bear it. Thus the reward of the muqallid's faith is not nullified even if he did not bear difficulty, because the absolute promise encompasses him. As for the faith of one who believes to repel punishment from himself, or was compelled to it, or after his soul left his hands, the text has come that it is not beneficial, so we said it does not benefit. And in the compelled case, this text is repelled, and the absolute promise for faith remains. And Shaykh Abu Mansur - may Allah have mercy on him - explained these three meanings for the deprivation of benefit of faith for one who believes at the sight of punishment. So upon this, this is an indication that the muqallid is not deprived of its benefit due to the absence of these meanings from him. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument defending the reward of the muqallid (one who believes without personal reasoning) by distinguishing his faith from the faith of one who believes only at the sight of punishment. The author begins by describing the difficulty of reaching true faith through reasoning (istidlal), requiring persistent reflection and bearing hardship. When a person exerts himself in this way for Allah's sake, he attains reward and the benefit of his faith. Conversely, if one seeks only immediate pleasures and believes without any hardship, he neither receives reward nor benefit from his faith, just as one who believes only when facing punishment does not benefit because he lacked prior reasoning. The author then argues that there is no distinction in reward between one who arrives at faith by reflecting on the created world (heavenly bodies, their temporality, the unity and attributes of the Creator, and prophethood) and one who arrives at it by reflecting on the signs and miracles of the prophets. Both involve hardship, so both receive reward even if the latter did not reflect on the cosmos. The author cites Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Imam al-Maturidi, who invoke the Quranic verse (6:158): 'On the day that some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith.' This verse is used to argue that faith at the time of punishment is not beneficial. The author then enumerates three reasons why faith at the time of punishment lacks benefit: (1) it is only to repel punishment, not genuine faith; (2) it is based on faith at the moment of punishment's attachment; (3) when worldly punishment occurs, it is a prelude to the Hereafter, and the soul has left the person's control. None of these conditions apply to the muqallid, because his faith is a voluntary act of drawing near to Allah, not a response to imminent punishment or compulsion. The muqallid's soul is still in his hands, and he is not forced. Since Allah's promise of reward for faith is general, the muqallid receives reward even without the hardship of reasoning. The author concludes that Imam al-Maturidi explained these three reasons to show that the muqallid is not deprived of reward, as the factors that nullify benefit are absent in his case.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The muqallid's lack of personal reasoning makes his faith invalid or unrewarded.
Correction: The passage argues that as long as his faith is not compelled or driven by fear of punishment, it is rewarded.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a faith to repel punishment, not genuine.
B) Because it is based on faith at the moment of punishment's attachment.
C) Because the person did not reflect on the cosmos.
D) Because the soul leaves the person's control.

Key Takeaway
The muqallid's faith is rewarded because it is not motivated by fear of punishment or compulsion, unlike faith at the time of punishment.

The Muqallid: Believer and Sinner
States that the muqallid is a believer and obedient in belief, but sinful for abandoning reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi school regards the muqallid as a valid believer yet accountable for not seeking evidence.

Core Idea
Faith without proof is valid but comes with a duty to reason.

What is the religious status of someone who believes without having examined the evidence? This passage from Imam al-Nasafi gives a precise answer: such a person is a true believer, but he is also sinful for abandoning his obligation to reflect. Let's examine the ruling closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: muqallid, mu'min, 'asi, nazar, istidlal.
The passage is a single sentence with several clauses.
2
Identify the two parts of the ruling
The passage gives two statements about the muqallid: one affirming his faith and obedience, and another stating his sin. Find these in the text.
Look for 'mumin' and 'asi'.
3
Understand the balance
Ask yourself: How can someone be both obedient and disobedient at the same time? The answer lies in the different aspects of religious obligation.
The muqallid is obedient in belief but disobedient in neglecting reasoning.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters. It protects the Islamic status of the common believer while upholding the duty of seeking knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا المذهب أن المقلد الذي لا دليل معه مؤمن، وحكم الإسلام له لازم، وهو مطيع الله تعالى باعتقاده وسائر طاعاته، وإن كان عاصيا بترك النظر والاستدلال،
And this is the madhhab: that the muqallid who has no proof with him is a believer, and the ruling of Islam applies to him, and he is obedient to Allah Most High by his belief and all his other acts of obedience, although he is disobedient by abandoning reflection and reasoning.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a concise doctrinal ruling on the status of the muqallid (the one who follows without evidence). It states the position (madhhab) of the school: the muqallid who does not possess a rational proof (daliil) for his beliefs is nonetheless a believer (mu'min). The legal rulings of Islam (ahkam al-Islam) are binding upon him, and he is considered obedient to Allah in his acts of belief and other acts of worship. However, he is also sinful (asi) for neglecting his duty to engage in personal reflection (nazar) and reasoning (istidlal). This ruling balances two aspects: the muqallid's faith is valid and he is a Muslim, but he is not excused from the obligation to seek knowledge through evidence. The passage does not specify the degree of sin or whether it is minor or major, but clearly affirms both his Islamic status and his culpability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: The passage affirms his faith while still holding him accountable for not seeking evidence.

C) He is a believer but sinful for abandoning reflection and reasoning.
D) He is not responsible for seeking proof.

Key Takeaway
The muqallid is a valid believer but sins if he neglects his duty to reason and seek evidence.

?
This passage balances mercy (faith is valid) and accountability (sin for not reasoning). Which side do you lean on? Do you use the mercy as an excuse to neglect seeking knowledge? Or do you become too harsh on yourself or others? How can you strike the balance in your own spiritual life?
